All things were made by him; and without him was not any thing made that was made. In him was life; and the life was the light of men. And the light shineth in darkness; and the darkness comprehended it not. There was a man sent from God, whose name was John. The same came for a witness, to bear witness of the Light, that all men through him might believe. He was not that Light, but was sent to bear witness of that Light. That was the true Light, which lighteth every man that cometh into the world. He was in the world, and the world was made by him, and the world knew him not. He came unto his own, and his own received him not. But as many as received him, to them gave he power to become the sons of God, even to them that believe on his name: Which were born, not of blood, nor of the will of the flesh, nor of the will of man, but of God. And the Word was made flesh, and dwelt among us, (and we beheld his glory, the glory as of the only begotten of the Father,) full of grace and truth."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Teológicos:**

| Término | Definición | Contexto |
|:---|:---|:---|
| *Word (Logos)* | Palabra, razón, principio divino | *"In the beginning was the Word"* |
| *comprehended* | entendió, captó | *"the darkness comprehended it not"* |
| *witness* | testigo | *"came for a witness"* |
| *lighteth* | ilumina | *"which lighteth every man"* |
| *own* | lo propio | *"came unto his own"* |
| *power* | autoridad, potestad | *"gave he power to become the sons of God"* |
| *flesh* | carne, humanidad | *"the Word was made flesh"* |
| *dwelleth* | habita, mora | *"dwelt among us"* |
| *beheld* | contemplaron, vieron | *"we beheld his glory"* |
| *only begotten* | unigénito | *"only begotten of the Father"* |
| *grace* | gracia | *"full of grace and truth"* |

**Figuras Retóricas en el Texto:**

| Figura Retórica | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **Paralelismo** | Estructura repetitiva | *"In the beginning was the Word, and the Word was with God, and the Word was God."* |
| **Inclusio** | Repetición de una palabra o frase al inicio y al final | *"In the beginning"* (v. 1) y *"in the beginning"* (v. 2) |
| **Quiasmo** | Estructura A-B-B-A | *"The Word was with God, and the Word was God"* |
| **Antítesis** | Contraste de ideas | *"light" vs. "darkness"* |
| **Metáfora** | Imagen teológica | *"Word" (Logos), "light," "life"* |
| **Hipérbole** | Exageración retórica | *"All things were made by him"* |
| **Anáfora** | Repetición de "and" (coordinación) | *"And... and... and..."* |
| **Sinécdoque** | La parte por el todo | *"flesh"* (por humanidad) |
| **Eufemismo** | Sustitución suave | *"his own"* (por el pueblo judío) |
| **Ironía** | Contraste entre expectativa y realidad | *"he came unto his own, and his own received him not"* |

**Análisis Estilístico:**

1. **Estructura del Prólogo:** El prólogo de Juan tiene una estructura de quiasmo e inclusio:
   - A: El Logos en el principio (vv. 1-2)
   - B: El Logos en la creación (v. 3)
   - C: El Logos como luz y vida (v. 4-5)
   - D: El testimonio de Juan (v. 6-8)
   - C': El Logos como luz verdadera (v. 9)
   - B': El Logos en el mundo (v. 10-11)
   - A': El Logos hecho carne (v. 12-14)

2. **Paralelismo:** El texto emplea un paralelismo cuidadoso. Los versículos 1-2 repiten el tema del Logos y su relación con Dios. El versículo 3 establece su papel en la creación, y los versículos 4-5 asocian el Logos con la vida y la luz.

3. **Antítesis:** La oposición entre luz y oscuridad es central al prólogo: *"the light shineth in darkness; and the darkness comprehended it not"*. Esta antítesis prepara el tema del conflicto cósmico entre el bien y el mal.

4. **Metáfora del Logos:** El uso del término *Logos* (palabra/razón) en el prólogo tiene profundas resonancias filosóficas y teológicas. En el contexto griego, el *Logos* era el principio racional del universo; Juan lo identifica con Jesús, estableciendo la encarnación.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Teológico):**

El estudiante debe escribir un ensayo teológico de 500-600 palabras sobre la encarnación del Logos en Juan 1:1-14.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The prologue to the Gospel of John stands as the most sophisticated theological statement of the New Testament. It opens with a bold assertion: "In the beginning was the Word" (1:1). The Greek term Logos, with its rich philosophical heritage, is deliberately employed to present Jesus as the divine principle of reason, order, and life. The prologue's structure is carefully crafted. The repeated use of "in the beginning" (vv. 1-2) echoes the opening of Genesis, establishing Jesus as the agent of creation. The parallel between the Logos and the Creator is reinforced by the claim that "without him was not any thing made that was made" (v. 3). The text then transitions to the Logos as the source of life and light (v. 4), with life being the light of humanity. The antithesis of light and darkness (v. 5) is a recurring theme in John's Gospel, setting the stage for the conflict between belief and unbelief. The introduction of John the Baptist (vv. 6-8) serves as a literary device to transition from the cosmic to the concrete. He is a witness to the light, but not the light itself. The true light (v. 9) is the Logos, who "lighteth every man that cometh into the world." This universal claim is then qualified by the historical reality: "He was in the world... and the world knew him not" (v. 10). The tragedy of rejection is articulated in verse 11: "He came unto his own, and his own received him not." This rejection is the context for the promise of grace and adoption: "as many as received him, to them gave he power to become the sons of God" (v. 12). The culmination of the prologue is the declaration of the incarnation: "the Word was made flesh, and dwelt among us" (v. 14). This phrase is the theological heart of the Gospel: the divine Logos assumes full humanity. The final clause, "full of grace and truth," echoes the Old Testament and establishes the messianic identity of Jesus. The prologue is a literary and theological tour de force, employing a range of rhetorical devices—parallelism, inclusio, antithesis, metaphor—to present the deepest claim of the Christian faith."*

**Edificación:** El prólogo de Juan es una obra maestra de la teología literaria, donde la belleza del lenguaje se une a la profundidad de la verdad.

---

### Lección 4 – "The Sermon on the Mount: Rhetoric and Moral Teaching"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis retórico de Mateo 5-7; uso de la antítesis, la hipérbole, la paradoja, la exhortación.

**Texto Base (KJV – Mateo 5:1-12, 38-48, extracto):**
> *"And seeing the multitudes, he went up into a mountain: and when he was set, his disciples came unto him: And he opened his mouth, and taught them, saying, Blessed are the poor in spirit: for theirs is the kingdom of heaven. Blessed are they that mourn: for they shall be comforted. Blessed are the meek: for they shall inherit the earth. Blessed are they which do hunger and thirst after righteousness: for they shall be filled. Blessed are the merciful: for they shall obtain mercy. Blessed are the pure in heart: for they shall see God. Blessed are the peacemakers: for they shall be called the children of God. Blessed are they which are persecuted for righteousness' sake: for theirs is the kingdom of heaven. Blessed are ye, when men shall revile you, and persecute you, and shall say all manner of evil against you falsely, for my sake. Rejoice, and be exceeding glad: for great is your reward in heaven: for so persecuted they the prophets which were before you. ... Ye have heard that it hath been said, An eye for an eye, and a tooth for a tooth: But I say unto you, That ye resist not evil: but whosoever shall smite thee on thy right cheek, turn to him the other also. ... Love your enemies, bless them that curse you, do good to them that hate you, and pray for them which despitefully use you, and persecute you; That ye may be the children of your Father which is in heaven."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Retóricos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *blessed* | bienaventurado, feliz, bendito |
| *poor in spirit* | humilde, pobre de espíritu |
| *mourn* | llorar, lamentarse |
| *meek* | manso, humilde |
| *hunger and thirst* | hambre y sed |
| *merciful* | misericordioso |
| *pure in heart* | puro de corazón |
| *peacemakers* | pacificadores |
| *persecuted* | perseguido |
| *revile* | insultar, vituperar |
| *resist not evil* | no resistir al malvado |
| *smite* | golpear, herir |
| *compel* | obligar, forzar |
| *enemies* | enemigos |
| *despitefully* | injuriosamente, afrentosamente |

**Figuras Retóricas en el Texto:**

| Figura Retórica | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **Antítesis** | Contraste de ideas en oraciones paralelas | *"Ye have heard... but I say unto you"* |
| **Paralelismo** | Estructura repetitiva | *"Blessed are... Blessed are..."* |
| **Anáfora** | Repetición de "Blessed" | *"Blessed are the poor... Blessed are they that mourn..."* |
| **Hipérbole** | Exageración | *"If thy right eye offend thee, pluck it out"* |
| **Paradoja** | Afirmación que parece contradictoria | *"Blessed are they that mourn"* |
| **Ironía** | Contraste entre apariencia y realidad | *"Blessed are the meek"* |
| **Exhortación** | Llamado a la acción | *"Love your enemies"* |
| **Inclusio** | Repetición de "Blessed" al inicio y al final | *"Blessed" (al inicio) y "Rejoice" (al final)* |
| **Quiasmo** | Estructura A-B-B-A | *"Mourn... comforted" / "hunger... filled"* |
| **Encadenamiento** | Conexión de ideas | *"hunger and thirst... righteousness... filled"* |

**Análisis Estilístico:**

1. **Estructura de las Bienaventuranzas:** Las bienaventuranzas siguen un patrón de tres partes: condición (ser pobre en espíritu), recompensa (el reino de los cielos), y conexión (porque sus atributos conducen a la bendición). El paralelismo es casi perfecto en cada una.

2. **Antítesis en las Antítesis:** La fórmula *"Ye have heard... but I say unto you"* es una antítesis retórica que establece la autoridad de Jesús sobre la ley. Cada antítesis presenta una interpretación radical de la ley.

3. **Hipérbole y Retórica:** El Sermón del Monte emplea hipérbole para enfatizar la seriedad de las enseñanzas morales: *"If thy right eye offend thee, pluck it out"*. Esta exageración no es literal sino retórica, diseñada para impactar y motivar.

4. **Exhortación y Motivación:** El sermón termina con una serie de exhortaciones que contrastan a quienes obedecen con quienes no: los sabios y los necios, la roca y la arena.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Retórico):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis retórico de 500-600 palabras del Sermón del Monte.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The Sermon on the Mount (Matthew 5-7) is the most comprehensive moral teaching of Jesus and a masterpiece of rhetorical persuasion. Its structure is deliberate. The Beatitudes (5:3-12) establish the character of the kingdom community: the poor in spirit, the meek, the merciful, the pure in heart. The use of the anaphoric 'Blessed are' creates a rhythmic incantation that invites the audience into a new moral universe. The Beatitudes are not commands but declarations; they describe who the citizens of the kingdom are. The central section of the sermon (5:21-48) presents a series of antitheses, each introduced by the formula 'Ye have heard... but I say unto you.' This structure is both rhetorical and theological. The 'you have heard' refers to the tradition, and 'but I say' establishes Jesus' authority as the interpreter of the law. Each antithesis intensifies the demand of the law, moving from external actions to internal dispositions: from not killing to not being angry, from not committing adultery to not looking with lust. The rhetorical strategy is to show that the law is not merely a set of external commands but a matter of the heart. The climax of the sermon is the exhortation to love enemies (5:43-48). This is the culmination of the moral teaching: the perfection of love that reflects the character of God. The use of hyperbole ('turn the other cheek,' 'go the second mile') serves to break the cycle of retaliation and to establish a new ethic of non-violence and generosity. The final section (7:1-29) concludes with a series of contrasts: the narrow way vs. the broad way, the good tree vs. the bad tree, the wise builder vs. the foolish builder. These contrasts are designed to provoke decision. The ultimate test of discipleship is not mere hearing but doing. The rhetorical power of the Sermon on the Mount lies in its ability to present a vision of the kingdom that is at once radical, demanding, and hope-filled."*

**Edificación:** El Sermón del Monte es el pináculo de la enseñanza moral de Jesús, donde la retórica y la teología se unen para ofrecer una visión del Reino.

---

### Lección 5 – Repaso: "The Word Became Flesh"
**Gramática focal:** Repaso del análisis literario y retórico de los textos estudiados en esta unidad.

**Actividad de Repaso:** El estudiante escribe un análisis comparativo de 600-700 palabras entre Génesis 1, Salmo 23 y Juan 1, comparando las estructuras literarias y teológicas de cada texto.

**Ejemplo de Análisis Comparativo:**

> *"The three texts studied in this unit—Genesis 1, Psalm 23, and John 1—represent distinct genres and theological perspectives, yet they share a common literary structure. All three begin with a statement of origin (creation, divine relationship, the Logos), move through a series of actions (creation, guidance, incarnation), and conclude with a declaration of blessing (goodness, dwelling in the house of the Lord, grace and truth). The literary devices employed reveal the theological intentions of each author. Genesis 1 uses parallelism and repetition to establish the authority of the Creator; Psalm 23 uses metaphor and imagery to express intimacy with God; John 1 uses abstract theological language to present the incarnation. The chiastic structure of Genesis 1 mirrors the movement from chaos to order; the structure of Psalm 23 mirrors the movement from provision to protection; the structure of John 1 mirrors the movement from transcendence to immanence. All three texts demonstrate the power of language to convey theological truth through literary form."*

---

## UNIDAD 2: EXÉGESIS Y HERMENÉUTICA AVANZADA
*Lecciones 6 a 10*

---

### Lección 6 – "The Old Testament and the New Testament: Intertextuality"
**Gramática focal:** Intertextualidad, tipología, alusión, citas del Antiguo Testamento en el Nuevo Testamento.

**Texto Base (Mateo 2:13-15, 17-18, citando Oseas 11:1 y Jeremías 31:15):**
> *"And when they were departed, behold, the angel of the Lord appeareth to Joseph in a dream, saying, Arise, and take the young child and his mother, and flee into Egypt, and be thou there until I bring thee word: for Herod will seek the young child to destroy him. When he arose, he took the young child and his mother by night, and departed into Egypt: And was there until the death of Herod: that it might be fulfilled which was spoken of the Lord by the prophet, saying, Out of Egypt have I called my son. ... Then was fulfilled that which was spoken by Jeremy the prophet, saying, In Ramah was there a voice heard, lamentation, and weeping, and great mourning, Rachel weeping for her children, and would not be comforted, because they are not."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Exegéticos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *typology* | tipología: interpretación de eventos del AT como prefiguraciones de eventos del NT |
| *intertextuality* | intertextualidad: la relación de un texto con otros textos |
| *fulfillment* | cumplimiento: la realización de la profecía en el NT |
| *quotation* | cita directa de un texto bíblico |
| *allusion* | alusión: referencia indirecta a un texto sin citarlo |
| *echo* | eco: resonancia de un texto en otro |
| *midrash* | interpretación rabínica del AT |
| *pesher* | interpretación que identifica el cumplimiento escatológico |

**Análisis de la Intertextualidad:**

1. **Éxodo y Oseas:** Mateo 2:15 cita Oseas 11:1 (*"Out of Egypt have I called my son"*). Esta cita se refiere originalmente al éxodo de Egipto, donde Israel fue liberado de la esclavitud. Mateo la aplica a Jesús, identificando a Jesús como el verdadero Israel que cumple la historia de la liberación.

2. **Jeremías 31:15:** Mateo 2:17-18 cita Jeremías 31:15 (*"Rachel weeping for her children"*). Originalmente, esta profecía se refería al exilio de las tribus del norte. Mateo la aplica a la matanza de los niños en Belén, identificando la tragedia de Belén con el lamento de Raquel. La profecía es interpretada como un cumplimiento tipológico.

3. **Tipología:** Mateo emplea la tipología para leer el Antiguo Testamento como una prefiguración de Cristo. Jesús es el nuevo Moisés (salvado en Egipto, llamado de Egipto), el nuevo Israel (como Israel, probado en el desierto), y el nuevo David (el Mesías).

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Exégesis):**

El estudiante debe escribir un ensayo exegético de 500-600 palabras sobre la intertextualidad de Mateo 2, analizando cómo el autor utiliza el Antiguo Testamento para presentar a Jesús como el cumplimiento de la historia de Israel.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"Matthew's Gospel opens with a genealogy that establishes Jesus as the legitimate heir of Abraham and David. This theme of fulfillment continues in the infancy narratives, where Matthew employs a technique of typological interpretation. The flight to Egypt (2:13-15) is interpreted through the lens of Hosea 11:1: 'Out of Egypt have I called my son.' In its original context, this passage refers to the exodus of Israel from slavery. Matthew reads this typologically: Jesus is the true Israel, who, like Israel, was called out of Egypt. The citation serves to establish Jesus as the embodiment of Israel's history. The lamentation of Rachel (2:17-18, citing Jeremiah 31:15) is similarly interpreted. Jeremiah's prophecy spoke of Rachel weeping for her children in exile. Matthew applies this to the slaughter of the innocents, seeing in the tragedy of Bethlehem a fulfillment of the prophetic word. The technique of typology does not merely identify similarities; it asserts that the events of Jesus' life fulfill the deeper meaning of the Old Testament. Matthew's use of intertextuality is not random; it is a deliberate theological program that demonstrates the continuity of salvation history. Jesus is not a new departure but the culmination of all that God has done in Israel."*

**Edificación:** La intertextualidad en Mateo muestra la unidad de la Escritura y la centralidad de Cristo en la historia de la redención.

---

### Lección 7 – "The Parables of Jesus: Literary and Theological Analysis"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis literario de las parábolas; parábola del sembrador, del buen samaritano, del hijo pródigo.

**Texto Base (KJV – Lucas 15:11-32, La Parábola del Hijo Pródigo):**
> *"And he said, A certain man had two sons: And the younger of them said to his father, Father, give me the portion of goods that falleth to me. And he divided unto them his living. And not many days after the younger son gathered all together, and took his journey into a far country, and there wasted his substance with riotous living. And when he had spent all, there arose a mighty famine in that land; and he began to be in want. And he went and joined himself to a citizen of that country; and he sent him into his fields to feed swine. And he would fain have filled his belly with the husks that the swine did eat: and no man gave unto him. And when he came to himself, he said, How many hired servants of my father's have bread enough and to spare, and I perish with hunger! I will arise and go to my father, and will say unto him, Father, I have sinned against heaven, and before thee, And am no more worthy to be called thy son: make me as one of thy hired servants. And he arose, and came to his father. But when he was yet a great way off, his father saw him, and had compassion, and ran, and fell on his neck, and kissed him. And the son said unto him, Father, I have sinned against heaven, and in thy sight, and am no more worthy to be called thy son. But the father said to his servants, Bring forth the best robe, and put it on him; and put a ring on his hand, and shoes on his feet: And bring hither the fatted calf, and kill it; and let us eat, and be merry: For this my son was dead, and is alive again; he was lost, and is found. And they began to be merry. Now his elder son was in the field: and as he came and drew nigh to the house, he heard musick and dancing. And he called one of the servants, and asked what these things meant. And he said unto him, Thy brother is come; and thy father hath killed the fatted calf, because he hath received him safe and sound. And he was angry, and would not go in: therefore came his father out, and intreated him. And he answering said to his father, Lo, these many years do I serve thee, neither transgressed I at any time thy commandment: and yet thou never gavest me a kid, that I might make merry with my friends: But as soon as this thy son was come, which hath devoured thy living with harlots, thou hast killed for him the fatted calf. And he said unto him, Son, thou art ever with me, and all that I have is thine. It was meet that we should make merry, and be glad: for this thy brother was dead, and is alive again; and was lost, and is found."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Literarios:**

| Término | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| *portion of goods* | herencia, parte de la hacienda | *give me the portion of goods* |
| *riotous living* | vida desenfrenada | *wasted his substance with riotous living* |
| *famine* | hambruna | *a mighty famine in that land* |
| *husks* | algarrobas, bellotas | *filled his belly with the husks* |
| *came to himself* | volvió en sí | *when he came to himself* |
| *hired servants* | jornaleros | *hired servants of my father's* |
| *have compassion* | tener compasión | *had compassion, and ran* |
| *fatted calf* | becerro engordado | *bring hither the fatted calf* |
| *merry* | alegre, contento | *make merry, and be glad* |

**Figuras Retóricas en la Parábola:**

| Figura Retórica | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **Alegoría** | Representación simbólica | *El hijo pródigo = pecador; el padre = Dios* |
| **Ironía** | Contraste entre expectativa y realidad | *El hijo que se fue es bienvenido; el hijo que se quedó está enojado* |
| **Paradoja** | Afirmación que parece contradictoria | *"Murió y ha vuelto a vivir"* |
| **Hipérbole** | Exageración | *"He would fain have filled his belly with the husks"* |
| **Personificación** | Atribución de características humanas | *"El padre... lo vio y tuvo compasión"* |
| **Diálogo** | Conversación directa | *El diálogo entre el hijo y el padre* |
| **Contraste** | Oposición de elementos | *"El hijo que se fue" vs. "el hijo que se quedó"* |

**Análisis Literario y Teológico:**

1. **Estructura Narrativa:** La parábola sigue una estructura de tres partes: el hijo que se va (vv. 11-16), el retorno (vv. 17-24), y la respuesta del hermano mayor (vv. 25-32). Cada parte presenta un drama teológico: la alienación, la reconciliación, y el juicio de la gracia.

2. **Personajes:** El padre representa a Dios; el hijo pródigo representa al pecador arrepentido; el hermano mayor representa a los fariseos y escribas que se ofenden por la gracia.

3. **Imágenes:** *"Cuando volvió en sí"* (v. 17) es una metáfora de la conversión. *"El padre lo vio... tuvo compasión... corrió"* (v. 20) es una imagen de la iniciativa de Dios en la salvación.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Literario-Teológico):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis de 500-600 palabras de la Parábola del Hijo Pródigo.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The Parable of the Prodigal Son (Luke 15:11-32) is one of the most profound literary and theological texts in the Gospels. It is a narrative masterpiece that operates on multiple levels. The story follows a classic three-act structure: departure, return, and response. The younger son's departure is a rejection of the father's love and a declaration of independence. The description of his wasteful life is not merely moral commentary but a statement about the consequences of sin. The turning point of the narrative is the phrase 'he came to himself' (v. 17), which marks the moment of repentance. The journey home is a movement from alienation to reconciliation. The father's response is the theological heart of the parable: he sees, runs, embraces, and kisses. This is a portrait of divine grace: God does not wait for the sinner to come all the way; He runs to meet him. The restoration of the son is marked by three symbols: the robe (dignity), the ring (authority), and the shoes (sonship). The celebration is a picture of the joy of heaven over the repentant sinner. The elder son's response introduces a counterpoint. His complaint reveals that he has served the father out of obligation, not love. The father's gentle rebuke concludes the parable: 'All that I have is thine' (v. 31). The meaning is twofold: grace is offered to both the rebellious and the self-righteous, and the joy of forgiveness is available to all who will receive it."*

**Edificación:** La Parábola del Hijo Pródigo es el clímax de la enseñanza de Jesús sobre la gracia de Dios, mostrando que el amor divino es incondicional y está disponible para todos.

---

### Lección 8 – "The Book of Revelation: Apocalyptic Literature"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis del género apocalíptico, simbolismo, estructura retórica y teológica.

**Texto Base (KJV – Apocalipsis 1:1-3, 9-20; 21:1-4):**
> *"The Revelation of Jesus Christ, which God gave unto him, to shew unto his servants things which must shortly come to pass; and he sent and signified it by his angel unto his servant John: Who bare record of the word of God, and of the testimony of Jesus Christ, and of all things that he saw. Blessed is he that readeth, and they that hear the words of this prophecy, and keep those things which are written therein: for the time is at hand. ... I, John, your brother and companion in tribulation, and in the kingdom and patience of Jesus Christ, was in the isle that is called Patmos, for the word of God, and for the testimony of Jesus Christ. I was in the Spirit on the Lord's day, and heard behind me a great voice, as of a trumpet, saying, I am Alpha and Omega, the first and the last: and, What thou seest, write in a book, and send it unto the seven churches which are in Asia... And I turned to see the voice that spake with me. And being turned, I saw seven golden candlesticks; And in the midst of the seven candlesticks one like unto the Son of man, clothed with a garment down to the foot, and girt about the paps with a golden girdle. His head and his hairs were white like wool, as white as snow; and his eyes were as a flame of fire; And his feet like unto fine brass, as if they burned in a furnace; and his voice as the sound of many waters. And he had in his right hand seven stars: and out of his mouth went a sharp twoedged sword: and his countenance was as the sun shineth in his strength. ... And I saw a new heaven and a new earth: for the first heaven and the first earth were passed away; and there was no more sea. And I John saw the holy city, new Jerusalem, coming down from God out of heaven, prepared as a bride adorned for her husband. And I heard a great voice out of heaven saying, Behold, the tabernacle of God is with men, and he will dwell with them, and they shall be his people, and God himself shall be with them, and be their God. And God shall wipe away all tears from their eyes; and there shall be no more death, neither sorrow, nor crying, neither shall there be any more pain: for the former things are passed away."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Apocalípticos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *revelation* | revelación (apocálipsis) |
| *signified* | comunicado por señales/símbolos |
| *prophecy* | profecía |
| *tribulation* | tribulación, aflicción |
| *patience* | paciencia, constancia |
| *candlesticks* | candelabros (las iglesias) |
| *Alpha and Omega* | primera y última letra del alfabeto griego |
| *countenance* | semblante, rostro |
| *new heaven and new earth* | nuevo cielo y nueva tierra |
| *tabernacle* | tabernáculo, morada |
| *dwell* | morar, habitar |
| *former things* | cosas pasadas |

**Figuras Retóricas y Símbolos:**

| Símbolo | Significado |
|:---|:---|
| *seven candlesticks* | las siete iglesias |
| *seven stars* | los ángeles de las iglesias |
| *Son of man* | Jesucristo |
| *white hair* | eternidad, pureza |
| *flame of fire* | juicio, poder |
| *fine brass* | fortaleza, resistencia |
| *sharp twoedged sword* | palabra de Dios |
| *new Jerusalem* | la iglesia glorificada |
| *bride* | la iglesia (esposa de Cristo) |
| *tears wiped away* | consuelo final |

**Análisis Literario y Teológico:**

1. **Género Apocalíptico:** La literatura apocalíptica se caracteriza por la revelación de secretos divinos, el uso de simbolismo, la visión de juicio y de restauración. Apocalipsis combina elementos de profecía, literatura visionaria y epistolar.

2. **Estructura:** El libro tiene una estructura quiástica que refleja el movimiento de la historia desde la iglesia presente hasta la consumación final.

3. **Simbolismo:** El simbolismo del libro es denso y multifacético. Cada símbolo tiene múltiples capas de significado, que deben interpretarse en su contexto histórico, literario y teológico.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Exégesis):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis de 600-700 palabras sobre la estructura y el simbolismo de Apocalipsis 1:9-20.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The vision of the Son of Man in Revelation 1:9-20 is a pivotal moment in the book. It establishes the authority of the vision and the identity of the revealer. John's location on Patmos is significant: exile and persecution are the context for the revelation. The description of the Son of Man is a densely layered intertextual tapestry, drawing from Daniel 7, Ezekiel 1, and the Old Testament theophanies. The seven golden candlesticks represent the churches, and the seven stars are the angels of the churches. The Son of Man's attributes are symbolic: the long robe signifies priestly dignity; the golden girdle signifies authority; the white hair suggests eternity and wisdom; the eyes of fire suggest penetrating judgment; the feet of brass suggest stability; the voice of many waters suggests power; the two-edged sword suggests the penetrating word of God; the countenance like the sun suggests glory. The vision is intended to evoke awe and comfort. The opening declaration, 'I am Alpha and Omega, the first and the last,' asserts the eternal sovereignty of Christ. The message to the churches is one of consolation and challenge: the risen Christ is with his people, and he holds the keys to death and hell. The vision serves as the foundation for the entire apocalyptic drama that follows."*

**Edificación:** El libro de Apocalipsis es una obra maestra de la literatura apocalíptica, llena de simbolismo y esperanza, que presenta la victoria final de Cristo sobre el mal.

---

### Lección 9 – "Paul's Rhetoric: The Art of Persuasion"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis retórico de Pablo: el uso de la antítesis, la diatriba, la exhortación, el pathos y el ethos en las cartas paulinas.

**Texto Base (KJV – Romanos 7:14-25):**
> *"For we know that the law is spiritual: but I am carnal, sold under sin. For that which I do I allow not: for what I would, that do I not; but what I hate, that do I. If then I do that which I would not, I consent unto the law that it is good. Now then it is no more I that do it, but sin that dwelleth in me. For I know that in me (that is, in my flesh,) dwelleth no good thing: for to will is present with me; but how to perform that which is good I find not. For the good that I would I do not: but the evil which I would not, that I do. Now if I do that I would not, it is no more I that do it, but sin that dwelleth in me. I find then a law, that, when I would do good, evil is present with me. For I delight in the law of God after the inward man: But I see another law in my members, warring against the law of my mind, and bringing me into captivity to the law of sin which is in my members. O wretched man that I am! who shall deliver me from the body of this death? I thank God through Jesus Christ our Lord. So then with the mind I myself serve the law of God; but with the flesh the law of sin."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Retóricos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *carnal* | carnal, natural, no espiritual |
| *sold under sin* | vendido bajo pecado (esclavo del pecado) |
| *allow not* | no apruebo, no hago |
| *consent unto the law* | estar de acuerdo con la ley |
| *dwelleth* | habita, reside |
| *to will* | querer, desear |
| *perform* | cumplir, hacer |
| *delight* | deleitarse, complacerse |
| *inward man* | el hombre interior |
| *warring* | luchando, guerreando |
| *captivity* | cautiverio |
| *wretched* | miserable, infeliz |
| *deliver* | librar |

**Figuras Retóricas en Pablo:**

| Figura Retórica | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **Antítesis** | Contraste de ideas | *"I would... I do not"* |
| **Paradoja** | Afirmación contradictoria | *"I delight in the law of God... but I see another law"* |
| **Diatriba** | Discurso retórico con preguntas retóricas | *"O wretched man that I am!"* |
| **Exclamación** | Expresión emocional | *"O wretched man that I am!"* |
| **Anáfora** | Repetición de palabras | *"For... For... For..."* |
| **Enumeración** | Lista de ideas | *"I delight, I see, I bring into captivity"* |
| **Pathos** | Apelación a las emociones | *"O wretched man that I am!"* |
| **Ethos** | Apelación a la autoridad moral del escritor | *"I know that in me... dwelleth no good thing"* |
| **Lugar común** | Tópico retórico | *"The good that I would I do not"* |

**Análisis Retórico:**

1. **Antítesis:** Pablo emplea la antítesis para mostrar el conflicto interno entre la mente y la carne. La repetición de "I would/I do not" crea una sensación de lucha y tensión.

2. **Diatriba:** El pasaje utiliza la diatriba, un estilo retórico que emplea preguntas retóricas y exclamaciones para involucrar al lector. La exclamación *"O wretched man that I am!"* (v. 24) es un momento de climax emocional.

3. **Pathos:** Pablo apela a las emociones del lector al describir su propia lucha interna. Esta vulnerabilidad crea empatía y establece un vínculo con el lector.

4. **Ethos:** Pablo establece su credibilidad al reconocer su propia impotencia. El reconocimiento de la debilidad humana crea un ethos de humildad y honestidad.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Retórico):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis retórico de 500-600 palabras sobre Romanos 7:14-25.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"Romans 7:14-25 is a masterpiece of Pauline rhetoric. The passage presents a vivid depiction of the human condition. The first-person narrative is not merely autobiographical; it is a rhetorical strategy to draw the reader into the experience of the struggle. The key rhetorical device is the pervasive use of antithesis. The contrast between 'I would' and 'I do not' (v. 15) is repeated and elaborated in vv. 16-20. This repetition is not merely stylistic; it is a theological argument about the nature of sin. The personification of sin as a dwelling entity ('sin that dwelleth in me') is a powerful metaphor that expresses the depth of human alienation. The dramatic climax is reached in v. 24: 'O wretched man that I am! who shall deliver me from the body of this death?' The exclamation is a rhetorical appeal to pathos, designed to provoke empathy and identification. The answer is given in v. 25: 'I thank God through Jesus Christ our Lord.' The transition from despair to gratitude is the movement from law to gospel. The final verse, 'with the mind I myself serve the law of God; but with the flesh the law of sin,' is a conclusion that captures the paradox of Christian existence. Paul's rhetoric is not merely persuasive; it is transformative. The passage does not leave the reader a passive observer; it invites him or her to enter into the struggle and to find hope in the deliverance that is in Christ."*

**Edificación:** Pablo utiliza la retórica para expresar la profundidad de la lucha humana y la certeza de la liberación en Cristo.

---

### Lección 10 – Repaso: "The Law and the Gospel"
**Gramática focal:** Repaso del análisis exegético y retórico de los textos estudiados en esta unidad.

**Actividad de Repaso:** El estudiante escribe un ensayo comparativo de 600-700 palabras sobre el uso de la intertextualidad, la tipología y la retórica en los textos del NT estudiados.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"This unit has explored the exegetical and rhetorical strategies of the New Testament. The intertextual use of the Old Testament in Matthew 2 demonstrates how the early church read the Old Testament typologically. The citation of Hosea and Jeremiah is not proof-texting but a theological interpretation that sees Jesus as the fulfillment of Israel's history. The parables of Jesus, particularly the Prodigal Son, employ narrative and allegory to convey theological truths in a form that is accessible and memorable. The Book of Revelation uses apocalyptic symbolism to express hope in the face of persecution. Paul's rhetoric in Romans 7 uses antíthesis and diatribe to express the tension between law and gospel. Each text employs literary devices that are appropriate to its genre and purpose, and each conveys a theological message that is as relevant today as it was in the first century."*

---

## UNIDAD 3: SINTESIS AVANZADA Y ESTILO LITERARIO
*Lecciones 11 a 15*

---

### Lección 11 – "The Song of Songs: Poetry and Sensuality"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis poético, metáforas, símil, sensorialidad en la poesía bíblica.

**Texto Base (KJV – Cantares 4:1-7):**
> *"Behold, thou art fair, my love; behold, thou art fair; thou hast doves' eyes within thy locks: thy hair is as a flock of goats, that appear from mount Gilead. Thy teeth are like a flock of sheep that are even shorn, which came up from the washing; whereof every one bear twins, and none is barren among them. Thy lips are like a thread of scarlet, and thy speech is comely: thy temples are like a piece of a pomegranate within thy locks. Thy neck is like the tower of David builded for an armoury, whereon there hang a thousand bucklers, all shields of mighty men. Thy two breasts are like two young roes that are twins, which feed among the lilies. Until the day break, and the shadows flee away, I will get me to the mountain of myrrh, and to the hill of frankincense. Thou art all fair, my love; there is no spot in thee."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Poéticos:**

| Término | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| *fair* | hermosa, bella | *thou art fair* |
| *doves' eyes* | ojos de paloma | *doves' eyes within thy locks* |
| *flock* | rebaño | *a flock of goats* |
| *shorn* | trasquilado | *even shorn* |
| *twins* | gemelos | *bear twins* |
| *barren* | estéril | *none is barren* |
| *thread of scarlet* | hilo de grana | *lips like a thread of scarlet* |
| *comely* | hermosa, atractiva | *speech is comely* |
| *temples* | sienes | *temples like a piece of a pomegranate* |
| *armoury* | arsenal | *tower of David builded for an armoury* |
| *bucklers* | escudos | *thousand bucklers* |
| *shields* | escudos | *all shields* |
| *roes* | gacelas | *two young roes* |
| *myrrh* | mirra | *mountain of myrrh* |
| *frankincense* | incienso | *hill of frankincense* |

**Figuras Retóricas en la Poesía:**

| Figura Retórica | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **Símil** | Comparación con "como" | *"Thy hair is as a flock of goats"* |
| **Metáfora** | Comparación directa | *"Thy lips are like a thread of scarlet"* |
| **Paralelismo** | Estructura repetitiva | *"Thy... thy... thy..."* |
| **Imaginería Sensorial** | Descripción de los sentidos | *"doves' eyes," "lips," "temples"* |
| **Personificación** | Atribución de características humanas a lo inanimado | *"the shadows flee away"* |
| **Hipérbole** | Exageración | *"a thousand bucklers"* |
| **Anáfora** | Repetición de "thy" | *"Thy teeth... Thy lips... Thy neck..."* |

**Análisis Estilístico:**

1. **Símil y Metáfora:** El texto emplea una serie de símiles y metáforas para describir la belleza de la amada: cabello como rebaño de cabras, dientes como ovejas, labios como hilo de grana. Cada imagen evoca una cualidad específica: la belleza natural, la pureza, la sensualidad.

2. **Imaginería Sensorial:** La imaginería es predominantemente visual y táctil. Los ojos, los labios, las sienes y el cuello son descritos con detalles que evocan la intimidad y la admiración.

3. **Estructura:** El poema sigue una estructura quiástica que se mueve desde la cabeza hasta los pies y luego regresa a la totalidad: *"Thou art all fair"*.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Poético):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis poético de 500-600 palabras sobre el Cantar de los Cantares 4:1-7.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The Song of Songs is the most passionate and sensuous book in the Bible. It celebrates the beauty of love in a series of highly vivid and metaphorical descriptions. In chapter 4, the beloved is addressed with a series of similes and metaphors that transform the human body into a landscape of desire. The language is intensely visual: 'doves' eyes,' 'a flock of goats,' 'a flock of sheep,' 'a thread of scarlet,' 'a piece of a pomegranate,' 'the tower of David.' Each image is chosen for its aesthetic and symbolic value. The hair is like a flock of goats—wild, abundant, and beautiful. The teeth are like a flock of sheep—uniform, clean, and harmonious. The lips are like a thread of scarlet—vivid, passionate, and desirable. The temples are like a pomegranate—fragrant, round, and inviting. The neck is like the tower of David—strong, noble, and protective. The breasts are like two young roes—tender, graceful, and life-giving. The repetition of 'thy' creates a rhythm of praise, a litany of admiration. The final line, 'Thou art all fair, my love; there is no spot in thee,' is a declaration of perfect beauty. The language is not merely descriptive; it is performative. It creates the beloved in the act of description. The theology of the Song is implicit: the love between the beloved and the beloved is a reflection of the love between God and Israel, Christ and the Church. The Song invites the reader to enter into the joy of love."*

**Edificación:** El Cantar de los Cantares es un poema que celebra la belleza y el poder del amor humano como reflejo del amor divino.

---

### Lección 12 – "The Prophetic Voice: Isaiah and the Rhetoric of Judgment and Hope"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis retórico de la profecía: juicio, esperanza, exhortación, y el uso de la imaginería y la ironía.

**Texto Base (KJV – Isaías 6:1-8):**
> *"In the year that king Uzziah died I saw also the Lord sitting upon a throne, high and lifted up, and his train filled the temple. Above it stood the seraphims: each one had six wings; with twain he covered his face, and with twain he covered his feet, and with twain he did fly. And one cried unto another, and said, Holy, holy, holy, is the Lord of hosts: the whole earth is full of his glory. And the posts of the door moved at the voice of him that cried, and the house was filled with smoke. Then said I, Woe is me! for I am undone; because I am a man of unclean lips, and I dwell in the midst of a people of unclean lips: for mine eyes have seen the King, the Lord of hosts. Then flew one of the seraphims unto me, having a live coal in his hand, which he had taken with the tongs from off the altar: And he laid it upon my mouth, and said, Lo, this hath touched thy lips; and thine iniquity is taken away, and thy sin purged. Also I heard the voice of the Lord, saying, Whom shall I send, and who will go for us? Then said I, Here am I; send me."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Proféticos:**

| Término | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| *throne* | trono | *sitting upon a throne* |
| *train* | cola, estela | *his train filled the temple* |
| *seraphims* | serafines (ángeles) | *Above it stood the seraphims* |
| *twain* | dos | *with twain he covered...* |
| *covered* | cubierto | *covered his face* |
| *fly* | volar | *he did fly* |
| *hosts* | ejércitos | *Lord of hosts* |
| *glory* | gloria | *full of his glory* |
| *posts* | umbrales | *posts of the door* |
| *smoke* | humo | *the house was filled with smoke* |
| *undone* | perdido, deshecho | *I am undone* |
| *unclean* | impuro | *unclean lips* |
| *live coal* | carbón encendido | *a live coal in his hand* |
| *altar* | altar | *from off the altar* |
| *iniquity* | iniquidad | *thine iniquity is taken away* |
| *purged* | purificado | *thy sin purged* |

**Figuras Retóricas en la Profecía:**

| Figura Retórica | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **Visión Teofánica** | Visión de Dios en majestad | *"I saw the Lord sitting upon a throne"* |
| **Santidad** | Repetición triples | *"Holy, holy, holy"* |
| **Imaginería de Juicio** | Imágenes de juicio y purificación | *"a live coal in his hand"* |
| **Exclamación** | Expresión emocional | *"Woe is me!"* |
| **Confesión** | Reconocimiento de pecado | *"I am a man of unclean lips"* |
| **Llamado** | Vocación divina | *"Whom shall I send?"* |
| **Respuesta** | Ofrecimiento voluntario | *"Here am I; send me"* |

**Análisis Retórico:**

1. **Vision de Gloria:** La visión de Dios en el trono establece la autoridad de la profecía. La descripción de los serafines enfatiza la santidad y majestad de Dios.

2. **Confesión y Purificación:** La reacción de Isaías es de terror y confesión. El carbón encendido es un símbolo de purificación; la iniquidad es quitada y el pecado es perdonado.

3. **Llamado y Respuesta:** La pregunta retórica *"Whom shall I send?"* es un momento de decisión. La respuesta de Isaías, *"Here am I; send me"*, es un modelo de disponibilidad.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Exegético):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis exegético de 500-600 palabras sobre Isaías 6:1-8, identificando la estructura y el significado teológico.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"Isaiah 6 is the call narrative of the prophet and a masterclass in prophetic rhetoric. The passage follows a classic pattern: theophany, confession, purgation, and commissioning. The theophany (vv. 1-4) describes the vision of God in terms of overwhelming majesty. The seraphim's triple repetition of 'holy' emphasizes the transcendence of God. The confession (v. 5) is a moment of profound self-awareness: the prophet recognizes his own moral inadequacy. The purgation (vv. 6-7) is a liturgical act of cleansing. The live coal from the altar is a symbol of divine purification; the forgiveness of sins is the precondition for prophetic ministry. The commissioning (v. 8) is a moment of decision. The prophet offers himself voluntarily. The passage is not merely a historical narrative but a theological declaration about the nature of prophetic ministry: it is grounded in the vision of God, the confession of sin, and the assurance of forgiveness."*

**Edificación:** La vocación de Isaías muestra que la profecía verdadera nace de la experiencia de la santidad de Dios y la confesión del pecado.

---

### Lección 13 – "The Book of Job: Theodicy and Dialogue"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis de la estructura dialogal, la retórica del lamento, la ironía y la teodicea.

**Texto Base (KJV – Job 38:1-7):**
> *"Then the Lord answered Job out of the whirlwind, and said, Who is this that darkeneth counsel by words without knowledge? Gird up now thy loins like a man; for I will demand of thee, and answer thou me. Where wast thou when I laid the foundations of the earth? declare, if thou hast understanding. Who hath laid the measures thereof, if thou knowest? or who hath stretched the line upon it? Whereupon are the foundations thereof fastened? or who laid the corner stone thereof; When the morning stars sang together, and all the sons of God shouted for joy?"*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Teológicos:**

| Término | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| *whirlwind* | torbellino, tempestad | *answered Job out of the whirlwind* |
| *darkeneth counsel* | oscurece el consejo | *darkeneth counsel by words* |
| *gird up thy loins* | ceñir los lomos (prepararse) | *gird up now thy loins* |
| *laid the foundations* | colocado los cimientos | *laid the foundations of the earth* |
| *measures* | medidas, dimensiones | *laid the measures thereof* |
| *stretched the line* | extendido la cuerda | *stretched the line upon it* |
| *fastened* | asegurado, fijado | *the foundations thereof fastened* |
| *corner stone* | piedra angular | *laid the corner stone* |
| *sang together* | cantaron juntos | *morning stars sang together* |
| *shouted for joy* | gritaron de alegría | *all the sons of God shouted for joy* |

**Figuras Retóricas en Job:**

| Figura Retórica | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **Ironía** | Contraste entre expectativa y realidad | *Job habla de su sufrimiento; Dios responde desde la creación* |
| **Pregunta Retórica** | Pregunta que no espera respuesta | *"Where wast thou?"* |
| **Exhortación** | Llamado a la acción | *"Gird up now thy loins"* |
| **Imaginería de Creación** | Descripción poética de la creación | *"laid the foundations of the earth"* |
| **Personificación** | Atribución de características humanas a lo inanimado | *"morning stars sang together"* |
| **Quiasmo** | Estructura A-B-B-A | *"Where wast thou? ... Who hath laid the measures?"* |
| **Paralelismo** | Estructura repetitiva | *"Where... Who... Whereupon... who"* |

**Análisis Literario y Teológico:**

1. **Estructura Dialogal:** El libro de Job está compuesto de diálogos entre Job y sus amigos, y finalmente entre Job y Dios. La estructura dialógica permite explorar diferentes perspectivas sobre el sufrimiento y la justicia divina.

2. **Preguntas Retóricas:** Dios responde a Job con una serie de preguntas retóricas diseñadas para mostrar la grandeza de Dios y la pequeñez de Job. Estas preguntas no son respuestas directas, sino un recordatorio de la majestad divina.

3. **Imaginería de Creación:** La respuesta de Dios se centra en la creación: la fundación de la tierra, las medidas del universo, la alegría de los seres celestiales. Esta imaginería es una afirmación de la soberanía de Dios.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Teológico):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis teológico de 600-700 palabras sobre Job 38, explorando cómo Dios responde al sufrimiento de Job.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The divine response to Job in chapter 38 is one of the most profound moments in the Bible. The text does not answer Job's questions about theodicy directly; instead, it reorients the entire problem. God speaks from the whirlwind, an image of power and mystery. The initial question is a rebuke: 'Who is this that darkeneth counsel by words without knowledge?' Job is not accused of wickedness but of ignorance. The divine speech that follows is a series of rhetorical questions that invite Job to contemplate the grandeur of creation. The effect is not to crush Job but to expand his vision. The questions move from the cosmic (the foundations of the earth) to the meteorological (the rain and the snow) to the animal kingdom (the wild donkey and the ostrich). God is not explaining His ways to Job; He is inviting Job to trust in His wisdom. The rhetorical questions are not demands for information but invitations to reflection. The implied answer to Job's suffering is not a logical explanation but a personal encounter. The final chapters of Job present a theophany that reaffirms God's sovereignty and invites Job to humility and trust. The restoration that follows is not a reward for Job's fidelity but a gracious gift of God."*

**Edificación:** El libro de Job es una exploración de la relación entre el sufrimiento humano y la soberanía divina, donde la fe no depende de la respuesta intelectual sino de la confianza en Dios.

---

### Lección 14 – "The Epistle to the Hebrews: Rhetoric of Superiority"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis retórico de la carta a los Hebreos: comparación y contraste, argumentación y exhortación.

**Texto Base (KJV – Hebreos 1:1-4):**
> *"God, who at sundry times and in divers manners spake in time past unto the fathers by the prophets, Hath in these last days spoken unto us by his Son, whom he hath appointed heir of all things, by whom also he made the worlds; Who being the brightness of his glory, and the express image of his person, and upholding all things by the word of his power, when he had by himself purged our sins, sat down on the right hand of the Majesty on high; Being made so much better than the angels, as he hath by inheritance obtained a more excellent name than they."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Retóricos:**

| Término | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| *sundry times* | en diversas ocasiones | *at sundry times* |
| *divers manners* | de diversas maneras | *in divers manners* |
| *fathers* | padres (antepasados) | *unto the fathers* |
| *prophets* | profetas | *by the prophets* |
| *heir* | heredero | *appointed heir of all things* |
| *brightness* | resplandor | *brightness of his glory* |
| *express image* | imagen exacta | *express image of his person* |
| *upholding* | sosteniendo | *upholding all things* |
| *purged* | purificado | *purged our sins* |
| *sat down* | se sentó | *sat down on the right hand* |
| *Majesty* | Majestad | *the Majesty on high* |
| *inheritance* | herencia | *inheritance obtained* |
| *excellent* | excelente, superior | *more excellent name* |

**Figuras Retóricas en Hebreos:**

| Figura Retórica | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **Comparación** | Contraste entre el AT y el NT | *"spoken in time past... spoken unto us"* |
| **Paralelismo** | Estructura repetitiva | *"whom he hath appointed... by whom also"* |
| **Anáfora** | Repetición de "who" | *"Who being... who... when..."* |
| **Clímax** | Ascenso de intensidad | *"brightness of his glory... express image... upholding all things"* |
| **Inclusio** | Repetición de "Son" | *"spoken unto us by his Son... hath by inheritance obtained"* |
| **Epíteto** | Descripción calificativa | *"brightness of his glory"* |
| **Exhortación** | Llamado a la acción | *(implícito en el contraste)* |

**Análisis Retórico:**

1. **Comparación y Contraste:** La carta a los Hebreos se construye sobre la comparación entre el Antiguo y el Nuevo Testamento. El autor enfatiza la superioridad de Cristo sobre los profetas (1:1-4), los ángeles (1:5-14), Moisés (3:1-6), y el sacerdocio levítico (capítulos 5-10).

2. **Argumentación y Exhortación:** Hebreos combina argumentación teológica con exhortación moral. La superioridad de Cristo es el fundamento para la fidelidad y la perseverancia.

3. **Climax:** El versículo 4 presenta un clímax: *"Being made so much better than the angels, as he hath by inheritance obtained a more excellent name than they."* Esta es la declaración culminante del prólogo.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Retórico):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis retórico de 500-600 palabras sobre Hebreos 1:1-4.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The opening verses of Hebrews present a rhetorical tour de force. The author establishes the theme of the entire epistle: the superiority of Christ. The structure is deliberate. The first clause, 'God, who at sundry times and in divers manners spake in time past unto the fathers by the prophets,' sets up the Old Testament as a period of partial and varied revelation. The second clause, 'Hath in these last days spoken unto us by his Son,' declares the definitive and final revelation in Christ. The contrast is not merely temporal but qualitative. The Son is described in a series of ascending appositives: 'whom he hath appointed heir of all things,' 'by whom also he made the worlds,' 'being the brightness of his glory,' 'the express image of his person,' 'upholding all things by the word of his power.' This ascending rhetoric prepares the listener for the climactic declaration: 'when he had by himself purged our sins, sat down on the right hand of the Majesty on high.' The motif of sitting at the right hand is a reference to Psalm 110, which is the most frequently cited psalm in the New Testament. The conclusion of the prologue, 'Being made so much better than the angels, as he hath by inheritance obtained a more excellent name than they,' introduces the theme of the Son's superiority to angels. The epistle's rhetoric is not merely persuasive; it is theologically constitutive. It creates a new understanding of the relationship between the Old and New Covenants."*

**Edificación:** La carta a los Hebreos demuestra la superioridad de Cristo sobre todas las formas anteriores de revelación divina.

---

### Lección 15 – Repaso: "The Prophetic Voice and the Epistolary Tradition"
**Actividad de Repaso:** El estudiante escribe un ensayo comparativo de 700-800 palabras sobre las estrategias retóricas empleadas en el Antiguo y Nuevo Testamento, comparando los textos estudiados en esta unidad.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"This unit has explored the rhetorical strategies of the prophetic, poetic, and epistolary traditions. Isaiah 6 presents a prophetic call narrative that employs vision, confession, and commissioning. The Song of Songs uses metaphor and sensuous language to express the beauty of love. Job 38 uses dialogue and rhetorical questions to explore the problem of suffering. Hebrews 1 uses comparison and contrast to establish the superiority of Christ. Each text employs distinctive rhetorical strategies that are appropriate to its genre and purpose. The prophetic tradition uses vision and exhortation; the poetic tradition uses metaphor and sensuality; the narrative tradition uses dialogue and irony; the epistolary tradition uses argumentation and exhortation. Together, these texts demonstrate the diversity and sophistication of biblical rhetoric."*

---

## UNIDAD 4: EXÉGESIS TEOLÓGICA Y FILOSÓFICA
*Lecciones 16 a 20*

---

### Lección 16 – "The Doctrine of the Trinity: Exegesis and Interpretation"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis exegético de los textos trinitarios; interpretación de Mateo 28:19, 2 Corintios 13:14, Juan 14-17.

**Texto Base (KJV – Mateo 28:18-20):**
> *"And Jesus came and spake unto them, saying, All power is given unto me in heaven and in earth. Go ye therefore, and teach all nations, baptizing them in the name of the Father, and of the Son, and of the Holy Ghost: Teaching them to observe all things whatsoever I have commanded you: and, lo, I am with you alway, even unto the end of the world. Amen."*

**Texto Base (KJV – 2 Corintios 13:14):**
> *"The grace of the Lord Jesus Christ, and the love of God, and the communion of the Holy Ghost, be with you all. Amen."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Teológicos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *power* | autoridad, poder |
| *nations* | naciones, todos los pueblos |
| *baptizing* | bautizando |
| *in the name of* | en el nombre de |
| *observe* | guardar, cumplir |
| *commanded* | ordenado |
| *alway* | siempre |
| *grace* | gracia |
| *love* | amor |
| *communion* | comunión, participación |
| *Holy Ghost* | Espíritu Santo |

**Análisis Exegético:**

1. **La Fórmula Bautismal:** Mateo 28:19 presenta una fórmula trinitaria: "en el nombre del Padre, y del Hijo, y del Espíritu Santo". La fórmula no es una enumeración de tres dioses sino una declaración de la participación de las tres personas en la obra de salvación.

2. **La Bendición de 2 Corintios 13:14:** La bendición paulina es una invocación trinitaria: la gracia de Cristo, el amor de Dios, y la comunión del Espíritu.

3. **Implicaciones Teológicas:** La doctrina de la Trinidad es la expresión de la naturaleza de Dios como comunidad de personas en relación.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Exégesis Trinitaria):**

El estudiante debe escribir un ensayo exegético de 600-700 palabras sobre la base bíblica de la doctrina de la Trinidad.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The doctrine of the Trinity is not a late invention of the church but is rooted in the New Testament witness. The baptismal formula in Matthew 28:19 is the clearest expression of the triune nature of God. The command to baptize 'in the name of the Father, and of the Son, and of the Holy Ghost' establishes a relationship between the three persons that is both distinct and unified. The singular 'name' indicates a single divine essence, while the threefold designation indicates distinct persons. This is not a mere formula; it is a theological statement about the nature of God. The Pauline benediction in 2 Corinthians 13:14 reinforces this understanding: 'The grace of the Lord Jesus Christ, and the love of God, and the communion of the Holy Ghost, be with you all.' The three elements are not interchangeable; they represent distinct aspects of the divine activity. The Gospel of John, particularly the Farewell Discourse (chapters 14-17), develops the relationship between the Father, the Son, and the Spirit. Jesus speaks of the Father sending the Spirit in his name, of the Spirit bearing witness to him, and of the Spirit glorifying him. This is not a modalistic or tritheistic view but a relational view of the triune God."*

**Edificación:** La doctrina de la Trinidad es el misterio central de la fe cristiana: un Dios en tres personas.

---

### Lección 17 – "The Problem of Evil: A Philosophical-Theological Analysis"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis filosófico-teológico del problema del mal; estudio de textos clave: Génesis 3, Job, Romanos 8.

**Texto Base (KJV – Romanos 8:18-25):**
> *"For I reckon that the sufferings of this present time are not worthy to be compared with the glory which shall be revealed in us. For the earnest expectation of the creature waiteth for the manifestation of the sons of God. For the creature was made subject to vanity, not willingly, but by reason of him who hath subjected the same in hope, Because the creature itself also shall be delivered from the bondage of corruption into the glorious liberty of the children of God. For we know that the whole creation groaneth and travaileth in pain together until now. And not only they, but ourselves also, which have the firstfruits of the Spirit, even we ourselves groan within ourselves, waiting for the adoption, to wit, the redemption of our body. For we are saved by hope: but hope that is seen is not hope: for what a man seeth, why doth he yet hope for? But if we hope for that we see not, then do we with patience wait for it."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Filosóficos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *reckon* | contar, considerar |
| *sufferings* | sufrimientos |
| *glory* | gloria |
| *revealed* | revelado |
| *earnest expectation* | expectativa ansiosa |
| *creature* | creación, criatura |
| *manifestation* | manifestación |
| *vanity* | vanidad |
| *subjected* | sometido |
| *bondage of corruption* | esclavitud de corrupción |
| *glorious liberty* | libertad gloriosa |
| *groaneth* | gime |
| *travaileth* | sufre dolores de parto |
| *firstfruits* | primicias |
| *adoption* | adopción |
| *redemption* | redención |
| *patience* | paciencia |

**Análisis Filosófico-Teológico:**

1. **El Problema del Mal:** El problema del mal es la tensión entre un Dios bueno y todopoderoso y la existencia del sufrimiento y el mal.

2. **La Respuesta de Pablo:** Pablo responde al problema del mal con una teología de la esperanza. El sufrimiento presente no es el final de la historia; hay una gloria futura que supera todo sufrimiento.

3. **La Creación en Dolores de Parto:** Pablo utiliza la metáfora de la creación que gime y sufre dolores de parto (vv. 22). Esta metáfora sugiere que el sufrimiento es el preludio de la nueva creación.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Filosófico-Teológico):**

El estudiante debe escribir un ensayo filosófico-teológico de 700-800 palabras sobre la teología del sufrimiento en Romanos 8.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"Romans 8 is the most comprehensive treatment of the problem of suffering in the New Testament. The opening statement, 'I reckon that the sufferings of this present time are not worthy to be compared with the glory which shall be revealed in us,' establishes the framework: present suffering is temporary and future glory is eternal. The 'hope' that Paul speaks of is not a vague optimism but a confident expectation grounded in the faithfulness of God. The language of 'groaning' and 'travailing in pain' is rich with meaning. The creation's groaning is a metaphor for the whole of created reality under the burden of sin and death. The hope of liberation is the hope of resurrection. The presence of the Spirit is the guarantee of this hope. Paul's theodicy is not a logical explanation but a theological affirmation: the suffering of the present is not the final word; God will restore all things. The hope of redemption gives meaning to present suffering and empowers believers to endure."*

**Edificación:** Romanos 8 es el himno cristiano a la esperanza, que transforma el sufrimiento presente en anticipación de la gloria futura.

---

### Lección 18 – "The Ethics of the Kingdom: Moral Teaching in the Sermon on the Mount"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis ético-teológico del Sermón del Monte; estudio de las bienaventuranzas y las antítesis.

**Texto Base (KJV – Mateo 5:13-16; 6:9-13):**
> *"Ye are the salt of the earth: but if the salt have lost his savour, wherewith shall it be salted? it is thenceforth good for nothing, but to be cast out, and to be trodden under foot of men. Ye are the light of the world. A city that is set on an hill cannot be hid. Neither do men light a candle, and put it under a bushel, but on a candlestick; and it giveth light unto all that are in the house. Let your light so shine before men, that they may see your good works, and glorify your Father which is in heaven. ... After this manner therefore pray ye: Our Father which art in heaven, Hallowed be thy name. Thy kingdom come. Thy will be done in earth, as it is in heaven. Give us this day our daily bread. And forgive us our debts, as we forgive our debtors. And lead us not into temptation, but deliver us from evil: For thine is the kingdom, and the power, and the glory, for ever. Amen."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Éticos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *salt of the earth* | sal de la tierra |
| *lost his savour* | pierde su sabor |
| *good for nothing* | bueno para nada |
| *trodden under foot* | pisoteado |
| *light of the world* | luz del mundo |
| *city on a hill* | ciudad sobre un monte |
| *candle* | vela, lámpara |
| *bushel* | celemín |
| *candlestick* | candelero |
| *shine* | brillar |
| *glorify* | glorificar |
| *hallowed* | santificado |
| *daily bread* | pan de cada día |
| *debts* | deudas (pecados) |
| *debtors* | deudores |
| *temptation* | tentación |
| *evil* | mal |

**Análisis Ético-Teológico:**

1. **La Sal y la Luz:** Las metáforas de la sal y la luz son imágenes de la función del discípulo en el mundo. La sal preserva y da sabor; la luz ilumina. Ambos son agentes de transformación.

2. **El Padre Nuestro:** El Padrenuestro es el resumen de la ética del Reino. La oración comienza con la adoración, se centra en el Reino, y culmina en la dependencia de Dios y el perdón.

3. **Las Bienaventuranzas:** Las bienaventuranzas son la descripción del carácter de los ciudadanos del Reino. Son declaraciones de bendición y promesa.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Ético-Teológico):**

El estudiante debe escribir un ensayo ético-teológico de 600-700 palabras sobre la ética del Sermón del Monte.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The Sermon on the Mount is the most comprehensive ethical teaching of Jesus. It presents the ethics of the Kingdom as a radical alternative to the ethics of the world. The metaphors of salt and light (5:13-16) emphasize the role of the disciples as agents of transformation. The salt of the earth is a symbol of preservation and flavor; the light of the world is a symbol of illumination and guidance. The image of the city on a hill is a metaphor for visibility and witness. The ethical teaching of the sermon is grounded in the character of God: the merciful, loving, and holy Father. The Sermon is a vision of a community shaped by the values of the Kingdom. The ethics of the Sermon is not a legalistic code but a call to discipleship that is grounded in the grace and mercy of God."*

**Edificación:** El Sermón del Monte es la presentación más completa de la ética cristiana, que llama a los discípulos a vivir como luz y sal en el mundo.

---

### Lección 19 – "The Apocalyptic Vision: Hope and Judgment"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis teológico del género apocalíptico; estudio de Daniel 7 y Apocalipsis 21-22.

**Texto Base (KJV – Daniel 7:13-14):**
> *"I saw in the night visions, and, behold, one like the Son of man came with the clouds of heaven, and came to the Ancient of days, and they brought him near before him. And there was given him dominion, and glory, and a kingdom, that all people, nations, and languages, should serve him: his dominion is an everlasting dominion, which shall not pass away, and his kingdom that which shall not be destroyed."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Apocalípticos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *night visions* | visiones nocturnas |
| *Son of man* | Hijo del Hombre |
| *clouds of heaven* | nubes del cielo |
| *Ancient of days* | Anciano de Días |
| *dominion* | dominio |
| *glory* | gloria |
| *kingdom* | reino |
| *everlasting* | eterno, perpetuo |
| *pass away* | pasar, desaparecer |
| *destroyed* | destruido |

**Análisis Teológico:**

1. **El Hijo del Hombre en Daniel:** La figura del Hijo del Hombre en Daniel 7 es una figura celestial que recibe dominio de parte del Anciano de Días. Esta figura es interpretada en el Nuevo Testamento como referida a Jesús.

2. **El Reino Eterno:** El reino que se da al Hijo del Hombre es un reino eterno, que no será destruido. Esta es la esperanza apocalíptica: un reino de justicia y paz.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Teológico):**

El estudiante debe escribir un ensayo teológico de 600-700 palabras sobre la esperanza apocalíptica en Daniel y Apocalipsis.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The apocalyptic literature of Daniel and Revelation presents a vision of hope in the midst of persecution and suffering. The vision of the Son of Man in Daniel 7 is a declaration of the sovereignty of God over history. The four beasts represent the empires of the world, and the Son of Man represents the kingdom of God. The victory of the Son of Man is not by military might but by divine intervention. The Book of Revelation develops this hope in a new key. The vision of the new heaven and the new earth (Revelation 21:1-4) is a vision of the consummation of all things. There will be no more death, sorrow, or pain. God will wipe away every tear from their eyes. The apocalyptic hope is not a resignation from the world but a confident expectation of God's ultimate victory."*

**Edificación:** La literatura apocalíptica ofrece esperanza en medio de la persecución, recordando a los creyentes que el Reino de Dios es eterno y triunfará.

---

### Lección 20 – Repaso: "Theology and Ethics in the Bible"
**Actividad de Repaso:** El estudiante escribe un ensayo de 800-900 palabras sobre la teología y la ética en el Antiguo y Nuevo Testamento, explorando la relación entre la fe y la práctica.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The Bible presents a unified vision of theology and ethics. Theology is not a set of abstract doctrines but a living relationship with God that shapes the moral life. The ethics of the Old Testament is grounded in the covenant: God's people are called to be holy because God is holy. The prophets call Israel to justice and righteousness, not merely as a legal requirement but as a response to God's grace. The Sermon on the Mount is the ethical heart of the New Testament: the ethics of the kingdom is a call to a righteousness that exceeds that of the scribes and Pharisees. The Apocalypse presents a vision of the final consummation of the kingdom of God, where justice and peace will reign. The relationship between theology and ethics is not one of priority but of integration. What we believe about God determines how we live. The Bible is a book of both revelation and transformation, calling us to know God and to become like him."*

---

## UNIDAD 5: RETÓRICA Y ESTILO AVANZADO
*Lecciones 21 a 25*

---

### Lección 21 – "The Psalms: Poetry, Praise, and Lament"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis de la estructura poética, el paralelismo, la metáfora, el lamento y la alabanza en los Salmos.

**Texto Base (KJV – Salmo 13:1-6):**
> *"How long wilt thou forget me, O Lord? for ever? how long wilt thou hide thy face from me? How long shall I take counsel in my soul, having sorrow in my heart daily? how long shall mine enemy be exalted over me? Consider and hear me, O Lord my God: lighten mine eyes, lest I sleep the sleep of death; Lest mine enemy say, I have prevailed against him; and those that trouble me rejoice when I am moved. But I have trusted in thy mercy; my heart shall rejoice in thy salvation. I will sing unto the Lord, because he hath dealt bountifully with me."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Poéticos:**

| Término | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| *how long* | ¿hasta cuándo? | *How long wilt thou forget me?* |
| *hide thy face* | esconder tu rostro | *hide thy face from me* |
| *take counsel* | tomar consejo, reflexionar | *take counsel in my soul* |
| *sorrow* | dolor, tristeza | *sorrow in my heart* |
| *exalted* | enaltecido | *mine enemy be exalted* |
| *consider* | atender, considerar | *Consider and hear me* |
| *lighten* | iluminar | *lighten mine eyes* |
| *prevailed* | prevalecido, vencido | *I have prevailed against him* |
| *rejoice* | alegrarse | *rejoice when I am moved* |
| *trusted* | confiado | *I have trusted in thy mercy* |
| *salvation* | salvación | *rejoice in thy salvation* |
| *bountifully* | abundantemente | *dealt bountifully with me* |

**Figuras Retóricas en los Salmos:**

| Figura Retórica | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **Pregunta Retórica** | Pregunta que no espera respuesta | *"How long wilt thou forget me?"* |
| **Paralelismo** | Estructura repetitiva | *"How long... How long... How long..."* |
| **Metáfora** | Comparación directa | *"hide thy face"* |
| **Exclamación** | Expresión emocional | *"How long wilt thou forget me?"* |
| **Antítesis** | Contraste de ideas | *"Lest mine enemy say... But I have trusted..."* |
| **Personificación** | Atribución de características humanas a lo inanimado | *"the sleep of death"* |

**Análisis Estilístico:**

1. **Estructura del Lamento:** El salmo sigue la estructura típica del lamento: una invocación (v. 1-2), una petición (v. 3-4), una afirmación de confianza (v. 5), y una promesa de alabanza (v. 6). La estructura permite al salmista pasar del dolor a la confianza.

2. **Paralelismo:** Las preguntas retóricas se estructuran en paralelismo, aumentando la intensidad emocional. La repetición de "How long" crea una sensación de urgencia.

3. **Personificación:** *"lighten mine eyes, lest I sleep the sleep of death"* es una personificación de la muerte como el sueño.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Poético):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis poético de 500-600 palabras sobre el Salmo 13.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"Psalm 13 is a classic example of the lament psalm. It begins with a repeated question—'How long?'—that expresses the tension between the psalmist's experience and his faith. The question is not merely rhetorical; it is an expression of deep anguish. The language is direct and personal: the psalmist addresses God directly, using the intimate second-person pronoun. The movement of the psalm is from lament to trust. The first two verses present the problem: God seems absent, the soul is in anguish, and the enemy is triumphant. The middle verses are a prayer for deliverance: 'Consider and hear me, O Lord my God.' The final verses move to a declaration of trust and a promise of praise: 'But I have trusted in thy mercy; my heart shall rejoice in thy salvation.' The transformation is not a change in circumstance but a change in perspective. The psalmist's faith is not dependent on his feelings; it is grounded in the character of God. The psalm ends with a commitment to praise: 'I will sing unto the Lord, because he hath dealt bountifully with me.' This is not a denial of suffering but an affirmation that God's faithfulness is greater than human experience."*

**Edificación:** Los Salmos nos enseñan a traer nuestras emociones a la presencia de Dios, confiando en su fidelidad incluso en medio del dolor.

---

### Lección 22 – "The Rhetoric of Paul's Letters: Argument and Exhortation"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis retórico de las cartas paulinas: el uso de la antítesis, la diatriba, y la exhortación en Gálatas y Romanos.

**Texto Base (KJV – Gálatas 5:16-26):**
> *"This I say then, Walk in the Spirit, and ye shall not fulfil the lust of the flesh. For the flesh lusteth against the Spirit, and the Spirit against the flesh: and these are contrary the one to the other: so that ye cannot do the things that ye would. But if ye be led of the Spirit, ye are not under the law. Now the works of the flesh are manifest, which are these; Adultery, fornication, uncleanness, lasciviousness, Idolatry, witchcraft, hatred, variance, emulations, wrath, strife, seditions, heresies, Envyings, murders, drunkenness, revellings, and such like: of the which I tell you before, as I have also told you in time past, that they which do such things shall not inherit the kingdom of God. But the fruit of the Spirit is love, joy, peace, longsuffering, gentleness, goodness, faith, Meekness, temperance: against such there is no law. And they that are Christ's have crucified the flesh with the affections and lusts. If we live in the Spirit, let us also walk in the Spirit. Let us not be desirous of vain glory, provoking one another, envying one another."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Retóricos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *walk in the Spirit* | andar en el Espíritu |
| *lust* | concupiscencia, deseo |
| *contrary* | contrario, opuesto |
| *led of the Spirit* | guiado por el Espíritu |
| *works of the flesh* | obras de la carne |
| *manifest* | manifiesto, evidente |
| *adultery* | adulterio |
| *fornication* | fornicación |
| *uncleanness* | impureza |
| *lasciviousness* | lascivia |
| *idolatry* | idolatría |
| *witchcraft* | hechicería |
| *hatred* | odio |
| *variance* | discordia |
| *emulations* | celos |
| *wrath* | ira |
| *strife* | contienda |
| *seditions* | sediciones |
| *heresies* | herejías |
| *envyings* | envidias |
| *murders* | homicidios |
| *drunkenness* | borracheras |
| *revellings* | orgías |
| *fruit of the Spirit* | fruto del Espíritu |
| *love* | amor |
| *joy* | gozo |
| *peace* | paz |
| *longsuffering* | paciencia |
| *gentleness* | benignidad |
| *goodness* | bondad |
| *faith* | fe |
| *meekness* | mansedumbre |
| *temperance* | templanza |
| *crucified* | crucificado |
| *affections* | pasiones |
| *desirous* | deseoso |
| *vain glory* | vanagloria |
| *provoking* | provocando |
| *envying* | envidiando |
