**Figuras Retóricas en Pablo:**

| Figura Retórica | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **Antítesis** | Contraste de ideas | *"flesh" vs. "Spirit"* |
| **Paralelismo** | Estructura repetitiva | *"love, joy, peace..."* |
| **Exhortación** | Llamado a la acción | *"Walk in the Spirit"* |
| **Enumeración** | Lista de ideas | *"works of the flesh... fruit of the Spirit"* |
| **Diatriba** | Estilo retórico dialogal | *"This I say then"* |
| **Condicional** | Estructura de "si" | *"If we live in the Spirit"* |

**Análisis Retórico:**

1. **Antítesis:** Pablo establece un contraste entre la carne y el Espíritu. La carne produce una lista de obras que son destructivas; el Espíritu produce un fruto que es constructivo. La antítesis es la estructura retórica principal.

2. **Enumeración:** Las listas de las obras de la carne y el fruto del Espíritu son ejemplos de enumeración retórica. La primera lista enfatiza la variedad del pecado; la segunda, la unidad de la virtud.

3. **Exhortación:** Pablo concluye con una exhortación a vivir en el Espíritu. La sección es una llamada a la acción.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Retórico):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis retórico de 600-700 palabras sobre Gálatas 5:16-26.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"Galatians 5:16-26 is a classic example of Pauline rhetoric. The passage employs a series of rhetorical devices to argue for a life lived in the Spirit. The initial command, 'Walk in the Spirit,' establishes the theme. The contrast between the flesh and the Spirit (v. 17) is the central antithesis. The enumeration of the works of the flesh (vv. 19-21) is a rhetorical catalog designed to evoke moral repulsion. The list of vices is not exhaustive but illustrative. The catalog of the fruit of the Spirit (vv. 22-23) is a positive contrast, emphasizing the virtues that mark the Spirit-filled life. The conclusion (vv. 24-26) is a series of exhortations. The passage is not merely a moral code but a rhetorical appeal to adopt a new identity. The logic is imperative: if one lives in the Spirit, one should walk in the Spirit. The rhetoric of Paul is not merely informative; it is transformative."*

**Edificación:** Pablo nos llama a vivir en el Espíritu, produciendo un fruto que refleja el carácter de Cristo.

---

### Lección 23 – "The Gospel of John: Theological Narrative"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis de la teología narrativa de Juan: el uso de la ironía, la ambigüedad y la revelación en los discursos de Jesús.

**Texto Base (KJV – Juan 6:25-40):**
> *"And when they had found him on the other side of the sea, they said unto him, Rabbi, when camest thou hither? Jesus answered them and said, Verily, verily, I say unto you, Ye seek me, not because ye saw the miracles, but because ye did eat of the loaves, and were filled. Labour not for the meat which perisheth, but for that meat which endureth unto everlasting life, which the Son of man shall give unto you: for him hath God the Father sealed. Then said they unto him, What shall we do, that we might work the works of God? Jesus answered and said unto them, This is the work of God, that ye believe on him whom he hath sent. They said therefore unto him, What sign shewest thou then, that we may see, and believe thee? what dost thou work? Our fathers did eat manna in the desert; as it is written, He gave them bread from heaven to eat. Then Jesus said unto them, Verily, verily, I say unto you, Moses gave you not that bread from heaven; but my Father giveth you the true bread from heaven. For the bread of God is he which cometh down from heaven, and giveth life unto the world. Then said they unto him, Lord, evermore give us this bread. And Jesus said unto them, I am the bread of life: he that cometh to me shall never hunger; and he that believeth on me shall never thirst."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Teológicos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *Rabbi* | Rabí, maestro |
| *verily, verily* | de cierto, de cierto (énfasis de Jesús) |
| *labour* | trabajar, esforzarse |
| *meat* | alimento (pan) |
| *perisheth* | perece, se echa a perder |
| *endureth* | perdura, dura |
| *everlasting life* | vida eterna |
| *sealed* | sellado |
| *believe* | creer |
| *sign* | señal, milagro |
| *manna* | maná |
| *bread of life* | pan de vida |
| *hunger* | hambre |
| *thirst* | sed |

**Figuras Retóricas en Juan:**

| Figura Retórica | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **Ironía** | Contraste entre apariencia y realidad | *La multitud busca a Jesús por el pan, pero él es el pan de vida.* |
| **Ambigüedad** | Multiplicidad de significados | *"bread of life"* (significado literal y metafórico) |
| **Metafora** | Comparación directa | *"I am the bread of life"* |
| **Paralelismo** | Estructura repetitiva | *"He that cometh... he that believeth"* |
| **Pregunta Retórica** | Pregunta que no espera respuesta | *"What sign shewest thou?"* |
| **Revelación** | Declaración divina | *"I am the bread of life"* |

**Análisis Teológico-Narrativo:**

1. **Ironía:** La multitud busca a Jesús por el pan que ha comido, pero Jesús ofrece el pan de vida que perdura para la vida eterna. La ironía es que la gente busca lo temporal y Jesús ofrece lo eterno.

2. **Metáfora:** La metáfora del "pan de vida" es una declaración de la identidad de Jesús. Es la revelación central del pasaje.

3. **Revelación:** El uso de la fórmula *"Verily, verily"* indica una revelación solemne. Jesús es el pan de vida que vino del cielo.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Teológico):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis teológico-narrativo de 600-700 palabras sobre Juan 6:25-40.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The discourse on the bread of life in John 6 is a theological masterpiece. The narrative is structured around the repeated formula 'Verily, verily,' which marks the solemn pronouncements of Jesus. The opening dialogue between Jesus and the crowd reveals the misunderstanding: the crowd seeks Jesus because he fed them, but they do not understand the true meaning of the sign. Jesus corrects their focus: they should not labour for the food that perishes but for the food that endures to eternal life. The statement 'I am the bread of life' is the theological climax of the discourse. The metaphor of bread is richly symbolic. Bread is the basic sustenance of life; Jesus is the sustenance of eternal life. The effect of the metaphor is to transform the understanding of the crowd. The passage is not merely a theological statement but a narrative that shapes the reader's understanding of who Jesus is and what he offers."*

**Edificación:** El Evangelio de Juan presenta a Jesús como el pan de vida que satisface la necesidad más profunda del ser humano.

---

### Lección 24 – "The Book of Acts: Narrative and Theology"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis de la narrativa de Hechos: estructura, retórica, y teología de la misión.

**Texto Base (KJV – Hechos 2:1-13):**
> *"And when the day of Pentecost was fully come, they were all with one accord in one place. And suddenly there came a sound from heaven as of a rushing mighty wind, and it filled all the house where they were sitting. And there appeared unto them cloven tongues like as of fire, and it sat upon each of them. And they were all filled with the Holy Ghost, and began to speak with other tongues, as the Spirit gave them utterance. And there were dwelling at Jerusalem Jews, devout men, out of every nation under heaven. Now when this was noised abroad, the multitude came together, and were confounded, because that every man heard them speak in his own language. And they were all amazed and marvelled, saying one to another, Behold, are not all these which speak Galileans? And how hear we every man in our own tongue, wherein we were born? Parthians, and Medes, and Elamites, and the dwellers in Mesopotamia, and in Judaea, and Cappadocia, in Pontus, and Asia, Phrygia, and Pamphylia, in Egypt, and in the parts of Libya about Cyrene, and strangers of Rome, Jews and proselytes, Cretes and Arabians, we do hear them speak in our tongues the wonderful works of God. And they were all amazed, and were in doubt, saying one to another, What meaneth this? Others mocking said, These men are full of new wine."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Teológicos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *Pentecost* | Pentecostés |
| *with one accord* | unánimemente |
| *rushing mighty wind* | viento impetuoso |
| *cloven tongues* | lenguas repartidas |
| *fire* | fuego |
| *filled with the Holy Ghost* | llenos del Espíritu Santo |
| *tongues* | lenguas (idiomas) |
| *utterance* | habla, expresión |
| *devout* | devoto, piadoso |
| *noised abroad* | difundido, esparcido |
| *confounded* | confundidos |
| *amazed* | asombrados |
| *marvelled* | maravillados |
| *Galileans* | galileos |
| *proselytes* | prosélitos |
| *mocking* | burlándose |
| *new wine* | vino nuevo |

**Análisis Narrativo:**

1. **Estructura:** El capítulo 2 de Hechos presenta la narrativa de Pentecostés: el evento del Espíritu, el testimonio de los discípulos, y la reacción de la multitud.

2. **Significado Teológico:** Pentecostés es el cumplimiento de la promesa de Jesús y el inicio de la misión de la iglesia. El Espíritu capacita a los discípulos para testificar en todas las lenguas.

3. **Reacción de la Multitud:** La reacción de la multitud es mixta: algunos se asombran y se preguntan; otros se burlan. Esta reacción prefigura la respuesta al evangelio a lo largo de Hechos.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Narrativo):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis narrativo-teológico de 600-700 palabras sobre Hechos 2:1-13.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The narrative of Pentecost in Acts 2 is a foundational text for understanding the nature of the church and its mission. The account is structured to emphasize the fulfillment of Old Testament prophecy and the empowerment of the disciples. The event begins with the descent of the Spirit: the sound of a rushing wind and the appearance of tongues of fire. This imagery is rich with Old Testament overtones. The wind recalls the Spirit of God moving at creation; the fire recalls the theophany at Sinai. The effect of the Spirit is immediate: the disciples speak in other tongues. This is not an ecstatic experience but a missional empowerment. The miracle is one of hearing: each person hears the disciples speaking in their own language. The message is the wonderful works of God. The reaction is mixed: some are amazed and ask what it means; others mock. The narrative sets the stage for Peter's sermon, which will explain the event in theological terms."*

**Edificación:** Hechos 2 es el relato del nacimiento de la iglesia, donde el Espíritu Santo capacita a los creyentes para ser testigos.

---

### Lección 25 – Repaso: "Rhetoric and Theology in the New Testament"
**Actividad de Repaso:** El estudiante escribe un ensayo de 800-900 palabras sobre la retórica y la teología en los textos del Nuevo Testamento estudiados.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The New Testament is a tapestry of rhetorical and theological expression. The Gospels use narrative and parable to convey the teaching of Jesus. The Pauline letters use argumentation and exhortation to address specific communities. The Book of Acts uses narrative to present the mission of the church. The Book of Revelation uses apocalyptic symbolism to offer hope. Each text employs literary devices appropriate to its genre and purpose. The rhetoric of the New Testament is not merely decorative; it is constitutive of its message. The language of the text shapes the reader's understanding and response. The theology of the New Testament is not abstract but embodied in the literary forms."*

---

## UNIDAD 6: LA BIBLIA COMO LITERATURA MUNDIAL
*Lecciones 26 a 30*

---

### Lección 26 – "The Influence of the Bible on English Literature"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis de la influencia bíblica en la literatura inglesa: Shakespeare, Milton, and modern literature.

**Texto Base (Shakespeare – "The Merchant of Venice" y "Macbeth"):**
> *"The quality of mercy is not strained; it droppeth as the gentle rain from heaven upon the place beneath."* (Merchant of Venice)
> *"Out, out, brief candle! Life's but a walking shadow, a poor player that struts and frets his hour upon the stage and then is heard no more."* (Macbeth)

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Literarios:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *quality* | calidad, esencia |
| *mercy* | misericordia |
| *strained* | forzado, restringido |
| *droppeth* | cae, gotea |
| *gentle rain* | lluvia suave |
| *brief candle* | breve vela |
| *walking shadow* | sombra que camina |
| *poor player* | pobre actor |
| *struts* | pavonea, se mueve con pompa |
| *frets* | se inquieta, se preocupa |
| *stage* | escenario |

**Análisis Literario:**

1. **Shakespeare:** Shakespeare es el escritor más influyente de la literatura inglesa. Sus obras están llenas de referencias bíblicas. La calidad de la misericordia en *El Mercader de Venecia* es una de las más famosas. La imagen del "breve candil" en *Macbeth* evoca la fugacidad de la vida humana.

2. **Milton:** *El Paraíso Perdido* es una epopeya bíblica. Milton se basa en el libro de Génesis y en la tradición cristiana para contar la historia de la caída de Adán y Eva.

3. **Literatura Moderna:** La literatura moderna está llena de referencias bíblicas: la novela de Steinbeck *Las uvas de la ira*, el poema de Eliot *The Waste Land*, la obra de Dostoyevsky *Los hermanos Karamazov*.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Literario):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis literario de 500-600 palabras sobre la influencia bíblica en la obra de Shakespeare.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"Shakespeare's work is saturated with biblical imagery and themes. The theme of mercy in The Merchant of Venice is directly linked to the biblical concept of mercy. The quality of mercy is 'not strained'—it is not forced, but freely given. This echoes the biblical teaching that mercy is an attribute of God and a call to the believer. The image of the 'brief candle' in Macbeth is reminiscent of the biblical theme of the brevity of life (Psalm 90:10, Job 14:1-2). The play's exploration of guilt and retribution echoes the biblical theme of divine justice. Shakespeare's use of biblical language is not merely decorative; it is integral to his literary and thematic purposes."*

**Edificación:** La influencia de la Biblia en la literatura inglesa es profunda y perdurable, dando forma a la lengua y la cultura.

---

### Lección 27 – "The Bible and the Art of Translation"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis de los desafíos y técnicas de la traducción bíblica; comparación de versiones (KJV, ESV, NIV, NASB).

**Texto Base (Comparación de Juan 3:16):**
> *"For God so loved the world, that he gave his only begotten Son, that whosoever believeth in him should not perish, but have everlasting life."* (KJV)
> *"For God so loved the world, that he gave his only Son, that whoever believes in him should not perish but have eternal life."* (ESV)
> *"For God so loved the world that he gave his one and only Son, that whoever believes in him shall not perish but have eternal life."* (NIV)

**Vocabulario y Conceptos de Traducción:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *only begotten* | unigénito |
| *believeth* | cree |
| *perish* | perecer |
| *everlasting life* | vida eterna |
| *one and only* | único |

**Análisis de Traducción:**

1. **KJV:** El *King James Version* es la traducción más influyente de la Biblia en inglés. Su lenguaje es poético y memorable, pero su vocabulario es arcaico.

2. **ESV:** La *English Standard Version* es una traducción literal y formal, que busca ser precisa y clara.

3. **NIV:** La *New International Version* es una traducción que busca equilibrio entre precisión y claridad.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis de Traducción):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis comparativo de 600-700 palabras sobre las diferentes versiones de la Biblia.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The translation of the Bible is a complex and demanding task. The differences between the KJV, ESV, and NIV reflect different philosophies of translation. The KJV is a formal equivalence translation that seeks to represent the Hebrew and Greek in a manner that is both accurate and dignified. The ESV is also formal equivalence but uses more contemporary vocabulary. The NIV is a dynamic equivalence translation that seeks to convey the meaning of the original in a way that is accessible to modern readers. The choice between these translations depends on the needs and preferences of the reader. The KJV is valued for its literary beauty; the ESV for its precision; the NIV for its clarity. Each translation has its strengths and weaknesses, and each serves a different purpose."*

**Edificación:** El arte de la traducción bíblica es un servicio esencial a la iglesia, que permite que la Palabra de Dios sea accesible a todas las naciones.

---

### Lección 28 – "The Bible and Modern Literature: Echoes and Allusions"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis de la influencia bíblica en la literatura moderna: Steinbeck, Faulkner, Dostoyevsky.

**Texto Base (Steinbeck – "The Grapes of Wrath"):**
> *"The last clear definite function of man—muscles aching to work, minds aching to create beyond the single need—this is man."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Literarios:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *function* | función, propósito |
| *aching* | doliendo, anhelando |
| *work* | trabajo |
| *create* | crear |
| *beyond* | más allá de |

**Análisis Literario:**

1. **Steinbeck:** La novela *Las uvas de la ira* está llena de simbolismo bíblico. La tierra prometida, el éxodo, y el juicio sobre la tierra son temas recurrentes.

2. **Faulkner:** Faulkner utiliza imágenes bíblicas para explorar temas de pecado, culpa y redención. La novela *El ruido y la furia* está llena de referencias bíblicas.

3. **Dostoyevsky:** La obra de Dostoyevsky está profundamente influenciada por el cristianismo ortodoxo. *Los hermanos Karamazov* explora temas de fe, duda y redención.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Literario):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis literario de 600-700 palabras sobre la influencia bíblica en una obra moderna.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"John Steinbeck's The Grapes of Wrath is a modern epic that draws heavily on the biblical exodus narrative. The Joad family's journey from Oklahoma to California parallels Israel's journey from Egypt to the Promised Land. The imagery of the drought, the migration, and the struggle for justice echoes the biblical themes of oppression and liberation. The character of Jim Casy is a Christ-like figure who sacrifices himself for the sake of the community. The novel's ending, with the family's hope for a new future, is a modern echo of the biblical hope of redemption. Steinbeck's use of the biblical narrative is not merely ornamental but integral to the novel's meaning."*

**Edificación:** La influencia de la Biblia en la literatura moderna demuestra la universalidad y la perdurabilidad de sus temas y su lenguaje.

---

### Lección 29 – "The Bible in World Literature: A Comparative Study"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis comparativo de la influencia bíblica en la literatura de diferentes culturas y épocas.

**Texto Base (Tolstoi – "Anna Karenina"):**
> *"The peace of God, which passeth all understanding, keep your hearts and minds in Christ Jesus."* (Cita de Filipenses 4:7)

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Literarios:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *peace* | paz |
| *passeth* | sobrepasa |
| *understanding* | entendimiento |
| *keep* | guardar |
| *hearts* | corazones |
| *minds* | mentes |

**Análisis Comparativo:**

1. **Tolstoi:** La obra de Tolstoi está profundamente influenciada por el cristianismo. La novela *Guerra y paz* y *Anna Karenina* están llenas de referencias bíblicas.

2. **Dante:** La *Divina Comedia* de Dante es una epopeya teológica que se basa en la visión cristiana del más allá.

3. **Borges:** Jorge Luis Borges utiliza imágenes bíblicas en sus cuentos, explorando temas de creación, redención y juicio.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Comparativo):**

El estudiante debe escribir un ensayo comparativo de 700-800 palabras sobre la influencia bíblica en dos o más textos de diferentes culturas.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The Bible has been a source of inspiration for writers across the globe. In Tolstoy's Anna Karenina, the opening line—'All happy families are alike'—can be read in the light of the biblical theme of love and forgiveness. In Dante's Inferno, the structure of hell is built on the biblical imagery of the afterlife. In Borges' The Library of Babel, the imagery of the infinite library echoes the theme of the infinite wisdom of God. Each writer draws on the Bible in a different way, reflecting the universality of biblical themes."*

**Edificación:** La influencia de la Biblia en la literatura mundial muestra la profundidad y el alcance de su mensaje.

---

### Lección 30 – Repaso: "The Bible and World Literature"
**Actividad de Repaso:** El estudiante escribe un ensayo de 900-1000 palabras sobre la influencia de la Biblia en la literatura mundial.

---

## UNIDAD 7: LENGUAJE Y ESTILO AVANZADO
*Lecciones 31 a 35*

---

### Lección 31 – "The Language of Prayer: Intimacy and Formality"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis lingüístico de la oración: el lenguaje de la intimidad, la súplica y la alabanza en los Salmos y las oraciones de Jesús.

**Texto Base (KJV – Juan 17:1-5):**
> *"These words spake Jesus, and lifted up his eyes to heaven, and said, Father, the hour is come; glorify thy Son, that thy Son also may glorify thee: As thou hast given him power over all flesh, that he should give eternal life to as many as thou hast given him. And this is life eternal, that they might know thee the only true God, and Jesus Christ, whom thou hast sent. I have glorified thee on the earth: I have finished the work which thou gavest me to do. And now, O Father, glorify thou me with thine own self with the glory which I had with thee before the world was."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos de Oración:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *lifted up his eyes* | levantó sus ojos |
| *hour* | hora |
| *glorify* | glorificar |
| *power over all flesh* | poder sobre toda carne |
| *eternal life* | vida eterna |
| *true God* | verdadero Dios |
| *finished the work* | terminado la obra |
| *glory* | gloria |
| *before the world was* | antes de que el mundo fuera |

**Análisis Lingüístico:**

1. **Intimidad:** El lenguaje de Jesús es personal y familiar. Él se dirige a Dios como "Padre". Esta es una expresión de intimidad y confianza.

2. **Súplica:** La oración es una súplica: "glorifica a tu Hijo". Jesús pide a Dios que cumpla su propósito.

3. **Alabanza:** La oración termina con una declaración de la obra completada: "He terminado la obra". Esto es un acto de alabanza y de afirmación de la fidelidad de Dios.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Lingüístico):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis lingüístico de 500-600 palabras sobre el lenguaje de la oración en Juan 17.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The prayer of Jesus in John 17 is one of the most intimate and profound prayers in the Bible. The language is marked by a deep intimacy with the Father. The use of the address 'Father' is significant. It is not a formal title but a personal term that expresses a unique relationship. The prayer is structured as a series of petitions and declarations. The central petition is 'glorify thy Son.' This is not a request for personal glory but a petition for the fulfillment of the divine purpose. The prayer moves from the work accomplished on earth to the eternal glory that existed before the world. The language of the prayer is both personal and cosmic. It reflects the unity of the Son with the Father and the mission of the Son in the world."*

**Edificación:** La oración de Jesús es un modelo de intimidad y confianza en el Padre.

---

### Lección 32 – "The Language of Prophecy: Vision and Declaration"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis lingüístico de la profecía: el lenguaje visionario, la declaración divina, y la exhortación en los profetas.

**Texto Base (KJV – Isaías 40:1-5):**
> *"Comfort ye, comfort ye my people, saith your God. Speak ye comfortably to Jerusalem, and cry unto her, that her warfare is accomplished, that her iniquity is pardoned: for she hath received of the Lord's hand double for all her sins. The voice of him that crieth in the wilderness, Prepare ye the way of the Lord, make straight in the desert a highway for our God. Every valley shall be exalted, and every mountain and hill shall be made low: and the crooked shall be made straight, and the rough places plain: And the glory of the Lord shall be revealed, and all flesh shall see it together: for the mouth of the Lord hath spoken it."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Proféticos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *comfort* | consolar |
| *warfare* | guerra, conflicto |
| *accomplished* | cumplido |
| *iniquity* | iniquidad |
| *pardoned* | perdonado |
| *wilderness* | desierto |
| *prepare* | preparar |
| *highway* | camino, calzada |
| *exalted* | exaltado |
| *made low* | abajado |
| *crooked* | torcido |
| *rough* | áspero |
| *revealed* | revelado |
| *mouth of the Lord* | boca del Señor |

**Análisis Lingüístico:**

1. **Declaración Divina:** *"Saith your God"* indica que la palabra es de Dios. La profecía es una declaración divina.

2. **Imaginería:** La imaginería de la preparación del camino, la exaltación de los valles y el allanamiento de los montes es una metáfora de la restauración.

3. **Revelación:** La gloria del Señor se revelará. La profecía es una promesa de la manifestación de la presencia de Dios.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Lingüístico):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis lingüístico de 500-600 palabras sobre Isaías 40:1-5.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"Isaiah 40 is one of the most poetic and comforting passages in the Bible. The opening words—'Comfort ye, comfort ye my people'—set the tone for the entire chapter. The language is marked by a divine imperative that is both a declaration and a promise. The phrase 'her warfare is accomplished' is a declaration of the end of the exile and the restoration of Jerusalem. The imagery of preparing the way in the wilderness is a metaphor for the coming of God's salvation. The exaltation of the valleys and the lowering of the mountains are images of the removal of obstacles. The final verse declares that the glory of the Lord will be revealed. The prophetic language is not merely descriptive but performative; it brings about what it declares."*

**Edificación:** La profecía es el lenguaje de la promesa divina, que transforma el futuro y ofrece esperanza.

---

### Lección 33 – "The Language of Wisdom: Proverb and Instruction"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis lingüístico de la literatura sapiencial: el proverbio, la instrucción, el refrán.

**Texto Base (KJV – Proverbios 1:1-7):**
> *"The proverbs of Solomon the son of David, king of Israel; To know wisdom and instruction; to perceive the words of understanding; To receive the instruction of wisdom, justice, and judgment, and equity; To give subtilty to the simple, to the young man knowledge and discretion. A wise man will hear, and will increase learning; and a man of understanding shall attain unto wise counsels: To understand a proverb, and the interpretation; the words of the wise, and their dark sayings. The fear of the Lord is the beginning of knowledge: but fools despise wisdom and instruction."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Sapienciales:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *proverbs* | proverbios, refranes |
| *wisdom* | sabiduría |
| *instruction* | instrucción, enseñanza |
| *perceive* | percibir, entender |
| *understanding* | entendimiento |
| *justice* | justicia |
| *judgment* | juicio |
| *equity* | equidad |
| *subtilty* | astucia |
| *simple* | simple, ingenuo |
| *discretion* | discreción |
| *increase learning* | aumentar el aprendizaje |
| *attain* | alcanzar |
| *counsels* | consejos |
| *interpretation* | interpretación |
| *dark sayings* | dichos oscuros, enigmas |
| *fear of the Lord* | temor del Señor |
| *knowledge* | conocimiento |
| *fools* | necios |
| *despise* | despreciar |

**Análisis Lingüístico:**

1. **Estructura:** El libro de Proverbios está estructurado como una serie de dichos sapienciales. La mayoría de los proverbios son de dos líneas, con paralelismo sinonímico o antitético.

2. **Función:** La función de los proverbios es transmitir sabiduría y enseñar al lector cómo vivir una vida justa y prudente.

3. **Temática:** La sabiduría se presenta como un don de Dios y un valor supremo. El temor del Señor es el principio de la sabiduría.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Lingüístico):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis lingüístico de 500-600 palabras sobre Proverbios 1:1-7.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The opening verses of Proverbs set the agenda for the entire book. The language is direct and didactic. The purpose of the book is stated explicitly: 'to know wisdom and instruction.' The terms used are multiple and overlapping: wisdom, instruction, justice, judgment, equity, subtilty. This is a literature of instruction that seeks to form character. The structure of the passage is marked by parallelism: 'wisdom and instruction,' 'justice and judgment.' The culminating verse—'The fear of the Lord is the beginning of knowledge'—is the theological foundation of the book. The fear of the Lord is not servile terror but reverential awe. It is the starting point for all true knowledge. The language of Proverbs is both personal and communal, calling the reader to respond to the wisdom of God."*

**Edificación:** Los Proverbios son una guía para vivir con sabiduría y discernimiento.

---

### Lección 34 – "The Language of Apocalypse: Symbol and Vision"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis lingüístico del lenguaje apocalíptico: simbolismo, visio, y profecía en el Apocalipsis.

**Texto Base (KJV – Apocalipsis 4:1-11):**
> *"After this I looked, and, behold, a door was opened in heaven: and the first voice which I heard was as it were of a trumpet talking with me; which said, Come up hither, and I will shew thee things which must be hereafter. And immediately I was in the spirit: and, behold, a throne was set in heaven, and one sat on the throne. And he that sat was to look upon like a jasper and a sardine stone: and there was a rainbow round about the throne, in sight like unto an emerald. And round about the throne were four and twenty seats: and upon the seats I saw four and twenty elders sitting, clothed in white raiment; and they had on their heads crowns of gold. And out of the throne proceeded lightnings and thunderings and voices: and there were seven lamps of fire burning before the throne, which are the seven Spirits of God. And before the throne there was a sea of glass like unto crystal: and in the midst of the throne, and round about the throne, were four beasts full of eyes before and behind. And the first beast was like a lion, and the second beast like a calf, and the third beast had a face as a man, and the fourth beast was like a flying eagle. And the four beasts had each of them six wings about him; and they were full of eyes within: and they rest not day and night, saying, Holy, holy, holy, Lord God Almighty, which was, and is, and is to come. And when those beasts give glory and honour and thanks to him that sat on the throne, who liveth for ever and ever, The four and twenty elders fall down before him that sat on the throne, and worship him that liveth for ever and ever, and cast their crowns before the throne, saying, Thou art worthy, O Lord, to receive glory and honour and power: for thou hast created all things, and for thy pleasure they are and were created."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Apocalípticos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *door was opened* | puerta abierta |
| *trumpet* | trompeta |
| *hither* | acá |
| *hereafter* | de aquí en adelante |
| *throne* | trono |
| *jasper* | jaspe |
| *sardine stone* | piedra de sardio |
| *rainbow* | arcoíris |
| *emerald* | esmeralda |
| *elders* | ancianos |
| *white raiment* | vestiduras blancas |
| *crowns of gold* | coronas de oro |
| *lightnings* | relámpagos |
| *thunderings* | truenos |
| *seven lamps of fire* | siete lámparas de fuego |
| *sea of glass* | mar de vidrio |
| *crystal* | cristal |
| *beasts* | seres vivientes |
| *full of eyes* | llenos de ojos |
| *six wings* | seis alas |
| *Holy, holy, holy* | Santo, Santo, Santo |
| *Almighty* | Todopoderoso |
| *glory* | gloria |
| *honour* | honra |
| *thanks* | acción de gracias |
| *worship* | adorar |
| *cast their crowns* | arrojar sus coronas |
| *worthy* | digno |
| *receive* | recibir |
| *pleasure* | voluntad, placer |

**Figuras Retóricas en el Apocalipsis:**

| Figura Retórica | Definición | Ejemplo |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **Simbolismo** | Uso de símbolos para representar realidades espirituales | *"seven lamps of fire"* = los siete espíritus de Dios |
| **Visión** | Descripción de una experiencia visionaria | *"I saw a throne set in heaven"* |
| **Paralelismo** | Estructura repetitiva | *"Holy, holy, holy"* |
| **Enumeración** | Lista de elementos | *"jasper, sardine stone, rainbow, emerald"* |
| **Personificación** | Atribución de características humanas a lo inanimado | *"they rest not day and night"* |
| **Exclamación** | Expresión emocional | *"Holy, holy, holy!"* |
| **Adoración** | Lenguaje de alabanza | *"Thou art worthy"* |

**Análisis Lingüístico:**

1. **Simbolismo:** El Apocalipsis es un libro de simbolismo profundo. Cada imagen tiene un significado teológico y espiritual. El trono es el símbolo del gobierno de Dios.

2. **Visión:** El lenguaje del Apocalipsis es visionario. Juan describe lo que ve, y sus visiones están llenas de significado teológico.

3. **Adoración:** El tema central del Apocalipsis es la adoración. Los seres celestiales adoran a Dios y al Cordero.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Lingüístico):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis lingüístico de 600-700 palabras sobre el lenguaje del Apocalipsis 4.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The language of Revelation 4 is a tapestry of symbolic imagery. The vision begins with a door opened in heaven, an image of divine revelation. The throne is the center of the vision. The description of the throne and its surroundings is layered and symbolic. The rainbow around the throne echoes the covenant of Genesis 9; the twenty-four elders represent the people of God; the seven lamps of fire represent the Holy Spirit. The four living creatures are reminiscent of Ezekiel 1 and symbolize the order of creation. The repeated cry 'Holy, holy, holy' is a Trinitarian declaration. The response of the elders is an act of worship. The language of the Apocalypse is not meant to be read as literal description but as symbolic vision. Each image is a doorway to theological understanding."*

**Edificación:** El Apocalipsis es un libro de adoración y esperanza, que revela la gloria de Dios y la victoria del Cordero.

---

### Lección 35 – Repaso: "The Language of the Bible: A Synthesis"
**Actividad de Repaso:** El estudiante escribe un ensayo de 900-1000 palabras sobre el lenguaje de la Biblia en sus diversos géneros: narrativa, poesía, profecía, apocalipsis.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The Bible is a library of diverse literary genres, each with its own linguistic characteristics. The narrative of Genesis uses a simple, repetitive style to tell the story of creation. The poetry of the Psalms uses metaphor and parallelism to express praise and lament. The prophecy of Isaiah uses vision and declaration to announce the coming of salvation. The apocalyptic vision of Revelation uses symbolism and imagery to reveal the end of history. Each genre employs linguistic strategies appropriate to its purpose. The Bible is a masterpiece of language, a book that speaks to the human heart in every generation."*

---

## UNIDAD 8: SINTESIS FINAL Y PRODUCCIÓN AVANZADA
*Lecciones 36 a 40*

---

### Lección 36 – "The Bible and the Human Condition: A Theological Reflection"
**Gramática focal:** Síntesis teológica y reflexión sobre la condición humana a la luz de la Biblia.

**Texto Base (KJV – Eclesiastés 3:1-8; Romanos 8:18-25):**
> *"To every thing there is a season, and a time to every purpose under the heaven: A time to be born, and a time to die; a time to plant, and a time to pluck up that which is planted; A time to kill, and a time to heal; a time to break down, and a time to build up; A time to weep, and a time to laugh; a time to mourn, and a time to dance; A time to cast away stones, and a time to gather stones together; a time to embrace, and a time to refrain from embracing; A time to get, and a time to lose; a time to keep, and a time to cast away; A time to rend, and a time to sew; a time to keep silence, and a time to speak; A time to love, and a time to hate; a time of war, and a time of peace."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *season* | tiempo, estación |
| *purpose* | propósito |
| *pluck up* | arrancar |
| *break down* | derribar |
| *build up* | edificar |
| *weep* | llorar |
| *laugh* | reír |
| *mourn* | lamentar |
| *dance* | bailar |
| *embrace* | abrazar |
| *refrain* | abstenerse |
| *rend* | rasgar |
| *sew* | coser |
| *silence* | silencio |
| *hate* | odiar |

**Análisis Teológico:**

1. **El Tiempo y la Eternidad:** Eclesiastés presenta la vida humana como una serie de tiempos y estaciones. Todo tiene su tiempo, pero el propósito divino trasciende el tiempo.

2. **La Condición Humana:** La Biblia presenta la condición humana como marcada por el pecado, el sufrimiento y la esperanza de redención.

3. **La Esperanza Cristiana:** La esperanza cristiana es la esperanza de la resurrección y la nueva creación.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Reflexión Teológica):**

El estudiante debe escribir una reflexión teológica de 700-800 palabras sobre la condición humana a la luz de la Biblia.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The Bible presents a comprehensive view of the human condition. Ecclesiastes 3 offers a poetic reflection on the rhythm of life: there is a time for everything. This is a recognition of the finitude of human existence. The human condition is marked by the limitations of time, the reality of suffering, and the presence of sin. Yet the Bible does not leave us in despair. Romans 8 speaks of a hope that goes beyond present suffering. The creation itself groans and waits for redemption. The human condition is redeemed through Christ. The hope of the believer is not in the circumstances of this life but in the promise of eternal life."*

**Edificación:** La Biblia ofrece una visión de la condición humana que reconoce el sufrimiento pero ancla la esperanza en la redención de Dios.

---

### Lección 37 – "The Bible and the Christian Worldview"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis de la cosmovisión cristiana según la Escritura: creación, caída, redención, consumación.

**Texto Base (KJV – Génesis 1:26-31; Romanos 8:18-25; Apocalipsis 21:1-4):**
> *"And God said, Let us make man in our image, after our likeness: and let them have dominion over the fish of the sea, and over the fowl of the air, and over the cattle, and over all the earth, and over every creeping thing that creepeth upon the earth. So God created man in his own image, in the image of God created he him; male and female created he them. And God blessed them, and God said unto them, Be fruitful, and multiply, and replenish the earth, and subdue it: and have dominion over the fish of the sea, and over the fowl of the air, and over every living thing that moveth upon the earth. And God said, Behold, I have given you every herb bearing seed, which is upon the face of all the earth, and every tree, in the which is the fruit of a tree yielding seed; to you it shall be for meat. And to every beast of the earth, and to every fowl of the air, and to every thing that creepeth upon the earth, wherein there is life, I have given every green herb for meat: and it was so. And God saw every thing that he had made, and, behold, it was very good. And the evening and the morning were the sixth day."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *image* | imagen |
| *likeness* | semejanza |
| *dominion* | dominio |
| *creeping thing* | reptil |
| *male and female* | varón y hembra |
| *blessed* | bendijo |
| *be fruitful* | fructificad |
| *multiply* | multiplicaos |
| *replenish* | llenad |
| *subdue* | sojuzgad |
| *dominion* | dominio |

**Análisis de la Cosmovisión:**

1. **Creación:** La creación es el fundamento de la cosmovisión cristiana. El mundo es creado por Dios y es bueno.

2. **Imagen de Dios:** La humanidad es creada a imagen de Dios, lo que establece la dignidad y el valor de cada persona.

3. **Dominio:** La humanidad recibe el mandato de tener dominio sobre la creación, lo que establece la responsabilidad ecológica.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis de Cosmovisión):**

El estudiante debe escribir un ensayo de 700-800 palabras sobre la cosmovisión cristiana a la luz de la creación.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The Christian worldview is grounded in the biblical narrative of creation. Genesis 1 presents a vision of a world that is created by God and declared to be good. The creation is not an accident but a purposeful act of divine love. The creation of humanity in the image of God is the climax of the narrative. This doctrine establishes the inherent dignity and value of every human being. The command to have dominion is not a license for exploitation but a call to responsible stewardship. The Christian worldview sees the world as a gift from God and the human person as a steward of that gift."*

**Edificación:** La cosmovisión cristiana está arraigada en la creación y la redención, ofreciendo una visión de la vida como un don de Dios.

---

### Lección 38 – "The Bible and Contemporary Issues: A Christian Perspective"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis de temas contemporáneos a la luz de la Escritura: ecología, justicia social, bioética, tecnología.

**Texto Base (KJV – Levítico 25:1-7; Miqueas 6:8):**
> *"And the Lord spake unto Moses in mount Sinai, saying, Speak unto the children of Israel, and say unto them, When ye come into the land which I give you, then shall the land keep a sabbath unto the Lord. Six years thou shalt sow thy field, and six years thou shalt prune thy vineyard, and gather in the fruit thereof; But in the seventh year shall be a sabbath of rest unto the land, a sabbath for the Lord: thou shalt neither sow thy field, nor prune thy vineyard. That which groweth of its own accord of thy harvest thou shalt not reap, neither gather the grapes of thy vine undressed: for it is a year of rest unto the land. And the sabbath of the land shall be meat for you; for thee, and for thy servant, and for thy maid, and for thy hired servant, and for thy stranger that sojourneth with thee, And for thy cattle, and for the beast that are in thy land, shall all the increase thereof be meat. ... He hath shewed thee, O man, what is good; and what doth the Lord require of thee, but to do justly, and to love mercy, and to walk humbly with thy God?"*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *sabbath* | sábado, descanso |
| *sow* | sembrar |
| *prune* | podar |
| *vineyard* | viña |
| *harvest* | cosecha |
| *groweth of its own accord* | crece por sí mismo |
| *reap* | segar |
| *grapes* | uvas |
| *undressed* | no podada |
| *servant* | siervo |
| *maid* | criada |
| *hired servant* | jornalero |
| *sojourneth* | habita como forastero |
| *cattle* | ganado |
| *beast* | bestia |
| *increase* | fruto, producto |
| *do justly* | hacer justicia |
| *love mercy* | amar misericordia |
| *walk humbly* | andar humildemente |

**Análisis de Temas Contemporáneos:**

1. **Ecología:** Levítico 25 presenta el principio del descanso sabático de la tierra. Este principio es una anticipación de la responsabilidad ecológica.

2. **Justicia Social:** Miqueas 6:8 resume la ética social: "hacer justicia, amar misericordia, y andar humildemente con Dios". Es un llamado a la justicia y la compasión.

3. **Bioética:** La teología de la imagen de Dios proporciona un marco para la bioética: el valor de la vida humana desde el momento de la concepción.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Contemporáneo):**

El estudiante debe escribir un ensayo de 700-800 palabras sobre la perspectiva cristiana sobre un tema contemporáneo.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The Bible offers a rich theological framework for addressing contemporary issues. The principle of the sabbath year in Leviticus 25 establishes the principle of rest for the land and the redistribution of resources. This principle is a precursor to the contemporary concern for ecological sustainability. The requirement in Micah 6:8—'to do justly, and to love mercy, and to walk humbly with thy God'—is a comprehensive statement of social ethics. It calls for justice, compassion, and humility. The doctrine of the image of God provides the foundation for bioethics: the value of human life is rooted in the divine image. Each of these principles offers guidance for addressing the challenges of our time."*

**Edificación:** La Biblia ofrece principios eternos que son relevantes para los desafíos contemporáneos.

---

### Lección 39 – "The Bible and the Future: Eschatology and Hope"
**Gramática focal:** Análisis de la esperanza escatológica en la Escritura: la consumación del reino de Dios.

**Texto Base (KJV – Apocalipsis 21:1-7; 22:1-5):**
> *"And I saw a new heaven and a new earth: for the first heaven and the first earth were passed away; and there was no more sea. And I John saw the holy city, new Jerusalem, coming down from God out of heaven, prepared as a bride adorned for her husband. And I heard a great voice out of heaven saying, Behold, the tabernacle of God is with men, and he will dwell with them, and they shall be his people, and God himself shall be with them, and be their God. And God shall wipe away all tears from their eyes; and there shall be no more death, neither sorrow, nor crying, neither shall there be any more pain: for the former things are passed away. And he that sat upon the throne said, Behold, I make all things new. And he said unto me, Write: for these words are true and faithful. And he said unto me, It is done. I am Alpha and Omega, the beginning and the end. I will give unto him that is athirst of the fountain of the water of life freely. He that overcometh shall inherit all things; and I will be his God, and he shall be my son. ... And he shewed me a pure river of water of life, clear as crystal, proceeding out of the throne of God and of the Lamb. In the midst of the street of it, and on either side of the river, was there the tree of life, which bare twelve manner of fruits, and yielded her fruit every month: and the leaves of the tree were for the healing of the nations. And there shall be no more curse: but the throne of God and of the Lamb shall be in it; and his servants shall serve him: And they shall see his face; and his name shall be in their foreheads. And there shall be no night there; and they need no candle, neither light of the sun; for the Lord God giveth them light: and they shall reign for ever and ever."*

**Vocabulario y Conceptos Escatológicos:**

| Término | Definición |
|:---|:---|
| *new heaven and new earth* | nuevo cielo y nueva tierra |
| *holy city* | ciudad santa |
| *new Jerusalem* | nueva Jerusalén |
| *bride* | esposa |
| *tabernacle* | tabernáculo, morada |
| *dwell* | morar, habitar |
| *wipe away* | enjugar |
| *tears* | lágrimas |
| *death* | muerte |
| *sorrow* | dolor |
| *crying* | llanto |
| *pain* | dolor |
| *former things* | cosas pasadas |
| *Alpha and Omega* | Alfa y Omega |
| *athirst* | sediento |
| *fountain* | fuente |
| *water of life* | agua de vida |
| *overcometh* | vence |
| *inherit* | heredar |
| *pure river* | río puro |
| *tree of life* | árbol de la vida |
| *healing* | sanidad |
| *nations* | naciones |
| *curse* | maldición |
| *foreheads* | frentes |
| *reign* | reinar |

**Análisis Escatológico:**

1. **Nueva Creación:** El Apocalipsis presenta la visión de un nuevo cielo y una nueva tierra. La creación será restaurada y renovada.

2. **No Habrá Más Muerte:** El fin de la muerte y el dolor es una de las promesas centrales.

3. **El Rey y el Reino:** Dios reinará eternamente. Los que han creído reinarán con él.

**Aplicación en Producción Escrita (Análisis Escatológico):**

El estudiante debe escribir un análisis escatológico de 700-800 palabras sobre la esperanza cristiana en el Apocalipsis.

**Ejemplo de Análisis:**

> *"The Book of Revelation concludes with a vision of hope. The new heaven and new earth are not a replacement of creation but a restoration. The imagery of the holy city coming down from heaven is a picture of God's presence with his people. The promise 'God shall wipe away all tears from their eyes' is the ultimate answer to human suffering. There will be no more death, sorrow, or pain. The tree of life reappears, and the nations are healed. The curse is removed, and God's servants will reign forever. This vision is not a fantasy but a promise. It is the hope that sustains the church in the present."*

**Edificación:** La esperanza cristiana es la esperanza de la nueva creación, donde Dios restaurará todas las cosas.

---

### Lección 40 – Repaso Final: "The Bible: God's Word to Humanity"
**Actividad Final de Evaluación:** El estudiante escribe un ensayo de 1000-1200 palabras sobre el tema: **"La Biblia como Palabra de Dios: Reflexión Teológica y Literaria"**, integrando todo lo aprendido en el curso.

**Ejemplo de Ensayo Final:**

> *"The Bible is the most influential book in human history. It is a library of diverse genres—narrative, poetry, prophecy, apocalypse—and a unified witness to the nature of God and the human condition. The literary richness of the Bible is inseparable from its theological depth. The narratives of Genesis establish the foundation of the Christian worldview: a good creation, a fallen humanity, and a God who acts to redeem. The poetry of the Psalms expresses the full range of human emotion—joy, sorrow, doubt, and faith—in language that is both personal and universal. The prophets speak with divine authority, calling the people to justice and hope. The Gospels present the life and teaching of Jesus, the climax of God's revelation. The Epistles offer theological reflection and ethical instruction. The Apocalypse provides a vision of the consummation of all things. The Bible is not a textbook but a living word that speaks to every generation. It is the story of God's love for his creation and the hope of redemption in Christ. To engage the Bible is to engage the Word of God."*

---

## Apéndice: Figuras Retóricas en la Biblia

| Figura Retórica | Definición | Ejemplo Bíblico |
|:---|:---|:---|
| **Metáfora** | Comparación directa | *"The Lord is my shepherd"* (Salmo 23:1) |
| **Símil** | Comparación con "como" | *"Thy hair is as a flock of goats"* (Cantares 4:1) |
| **Personificación** | Atribución de características humanas a lo inanimado | *"The mountains shall bring peace"* (Salmo 72:3) |
| **Hipérbole** | Exageración | *"If your right eye causes you to sin, pluck it out"* (Mateo 5:29) |
| **Paradoja** | Afirmación que parece contradictoria | *"For whoever wants to save their life will lose it"* (Marcos 8:35) |
| **Ironía** | Contraste entre apariencia y realidad | *"He saved others; he cannot save himself"* (Marcos 15:31) |
| **Antítesis** | Contraste de ideas | *"The Spirit against the flesh"* (Gálatas 5:17) |
| **Paralelismo** | Estructura repetitiva | *"Blessed are the poor... Blessed are they that mourn"* (Mateo 5:3-4) |
| **Quiasmo** | Estructura A-B-B-A | *"The first shall be last, and the last first"* (Mateo 19:30) |
| **Anáfora** | Repetición de palabras al inicio | *"He makes me... He leads me... He restores me..."* (Salmo 23:2-3) |
| **Epífora** | Repetición de palabras al final | *"...and it was so"* (Génesis 1) |
| **Inclusio** | Repetición de una frase al inicio y al final | *"The fear of the Lord is the beginning of wisdom"* (Proverbios 9:10) |
| **Eufemismo** | Sustitución suave | *"To sleep"* por *"to die"* (Juan 11:11) |
| **Sinécdoque** | La parte por el todo | *"Flesh"* por *"humanity"* (Juan 1:14) |
| **Metonimia** | Substitución por un término relacionado | *"The sword"* por *"war"* (Mateo 10:34) |
| **Alegoría** | Representación simbólica | *La Parábola del Sembrador* (Mateo 13) |
| **Imaginería** | Descripción de imágenes | *"The Lamb of God"* (Juan 1:29) |
| **Exclamación** | Expresión emocional | *"O wretched man that I am!"* (Romanos 7:24) |
| **Pregunta Retórica** | Pregunta que no espera respuesta | *"Who is this that darkeneth counsel?"* (Job 38:2) |
| **Diatriba** | Discurso retórico dialogal | *"You fool!"* (Mateo 5:22) |
| **Enumeración** | Lista de elementos | *"Love, joy, peace, patience..."* (Gálatas 5:22-23) |

---

## Conclusión del Curso

Al completar este nivel C2, el estudiante será capaz de:

- Comprender prácticamente todo texto bíblico en inglés, incluyendo versiones literarias (KJV, ESV, NIV, NASB), reconociendo significados implícitos, matices y alusiones.
- Expresarse con fluidez y precisión en cualquier contexto, desde la conversación informal hasta la predicación y la enseñanza teológica.
- Producir textos teológicos y literarios de alta calidad, utilizando un estilo formal o poético según sea necesario.
- Analizar y evaluar críticamente textos bíblicos y teológicos.
- Comprender la influencia cultural y literaria de la Biblia en la literatura mundial y el discurso contemporáneo.

**Edificación Final:**

> *"Y conoceréis la verdad, y la verdad os hará libres."* — Juan 8:32

El estudiante ha recorrido un camino desde el nivel A1 hasta el C2. Ahora puede leer la Biblia en inglés en cualquier versión con plena comprensión, puede discutir su fe con otros en inglés con precisión y elocuencia, puede enseñar, predicar y escribir en inglés, y puede seguir creciendo en el conocimiento de la Palabra. Este curso ha sido un instrumento para que la Palabra de Dios more abundantemente en su corazón en el idioma inglés.

**"Toda la Escritura es inspirada por Dios y útil para enseñar, para redargüir, para corregir, para instruir en justicia, a fin de que el hombre de Dios sea perfecto, enteramente preparado para toda buena obra."** – 2 Timoteo 3:16-17

---

**¡A Él sea la gloria en la iglesia y en Cristo Jesús por todas las generaciones, por los siglos de los siglos! Amén.** (Efesios 3:21)
